TITLE 3
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
CHAPTER 1
ZONING COMMISSION 1 , 2
SECTION:
3-1-1: Appointment; Terms
3-1-2: Powers And Duties
 
Notes
1 1. MCA § 76-2-307.
2 2. See also section
  12-1-9 of this code.
3-1-1: APPOINTMENT; TERMS:
There is hereby created a commission to be known as and designated the zoning
commission, which such commission shall consist of five (5) members to be
appointed by the mayor, one of whom must be a member of the city council and
the other four (4) may or may not be members of the city council at the
discretion of the mayor, but must be residents of the city. The effective date
of this section shall be the first regular meeting held by the city of Forsyth,
in the month of January 2003.
On the effective date hereof, the mayor shall appoint one member of said
commission to hold office for one year, and two (2) to hold the office for two
(2) years, and two (2) to hold the office for three (3) years; and thereafter
as the term of each such member expires, the mayor shall appoint a commissioner
for the term of three (3) years and until his successor is appointed.
Any commissioner, other than a city council member, may be discharged from the
office at any time for cause by the mayor with the concurrence of three (3)
other city council members.
In the event a commissioner is a city council member, and no longer serves in
that capacity, the appointment to the commission terminates upon their
departure from office. (Ord. 2002-12, 11-12-2002, eff. 12-12-2002)
3-1-2: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Rules And Regulations Established: The zoning commission shall adopt
such rules and regulations as it may deem necessary to carry into effect the
provisions and purposes of this chapter, and it shall hold such meetings and
meet at such places from time to time and have such hearings as the commission
or majority thereof may determine. At the first meeting of the commission, it
shall elect one of its members chairman, and then on May 1 of each year
thereafter, the commission shall meet and organize by electing a chairman to
serve as such chairman for one year. (1961 Code § 2-3-3)
   B.   Boundary Recommendations: Such commission shall recommend the
boundaries of the various original districts and regulations to be enforced.
(1961 Code § 2-3-4)
   C.   Keeping Of Records: The city clerk-treasurer may be ex officio clerk of
the zoning commission and keep its records and notify it of the filing of
applications for permits and such other matters that come before the
commission, and the commission shall, when there is business to transact, hold
a meeting at least once each month or more often, as the business of the
commission requires. (1961 Code § 2-3-2)
   D.   Required Reports: Such commission shall make preliminary reports and
hold public hearings thereon before submitting final reports to the city
council. Such city council shall not hold its public hearings or take action
until it has received the final report of such commission. (1961 Code § 2-3-5)
CHAPTER 2
TREE BOARD 1
SECTION:
3-2-1: Establishment
3-2-2: Term Of Office
3-2-3: Compensation
3-2-4: Duties And Responsibilities
3-2-5: Operation
3-2-6: Review By City Council
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 5, chapter 5 of this Code.
3-2-1: ESTABLISHMENT:
There shall be a committee known as the Tree Board of the City of Forsyth,
Montana. The members shall be appointed by the Mayor and approved by the City
Council. A majority of the members of the Tree Board shall be residents of the
City of Forsyth. The board shall consist of the following or a similar
composition:
   Mayor
   Two (2) members of the City Council
   One representative from the Public Works Department, City of Forsyth
   Members at large
(Ord. 2018-03, 12-10-2018)
3-2-2: TERM OF OFFICE:
The term of the voting members shall be:
   Mayor and two (2) Council Members: term of office
   One (1) Representative of Public Works: term set by Mayor
   Members at large: three (3) years
In the event that a vacancy shall occur during the term of any member, his
successor shall be appointed in the same manner as the original appointment for
the unexpired portion of the term. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005; amd. Ord. 2019-
02, 1-13-2020)
3-2-3: COMPENSATION:
Members of the board shall serve without compensation. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-
2005)
3-2-4: DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES:
It shall be the responsibility of the board to study, investigate, counsel and
develop and/or update annually a written plan for the care, preservation,
trimming, planting, replanting, removal or disposition of trees and shrubs in
public ways, streets and alleys. Included in the plan shall be appropriate
educational programs for the public. Such plan will be presented annually to
the City Council and upon their acceptance and approval shall constitute the
official comprehensive City tree plan for the City of Forsyth, Montana.
The City Tree Board, or its agent, shall be responsible for an ongoing
inventory of Forsyth's tree resources. This inventory shall consist of a
minimum yearly hazard tree assessment. Further, the City Tree Board shall
prepare, or have prepared, a 10-year master plan for Forsyth's tree resources.
This plan shall include an inventory of said resources, goals, objectives, long
term maintenance, planting, and removal goals.
The City Tree Board, or its agent, may be responsible for the supervising of
the planting, pruning, and removal of all trees located within the street
rights-of-way, easements, alleys and parks of the City. The owners of land
abutting on any street may, when acting within the provisions of this chapter,
prune, spray, plant or remove trees in that part of the street abutting the
owner's land not used for public travel. A street tree permit shall be required
only when the owner of the property intends to deviate from the rules and
regulations contained in this chapter.
The board, when requested by the City Council, shall consider, investigate,
make findings, report and recommend upon any special matter or questions coming
within the scope of its work. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
3-2-5: OPERATION:
The board shall choose its own officers at the first meeting of each year, make
its own rules and regulations and keep a journal of its proceedings. A majority
of the members shall be a quorum for the transaction of business. Officers are
Chair, Vice Chair, Secretary, and Treasurer. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
3-2-6: REVIEW BY CITY COUNCIL:
The City Council shall have the right to review the conduct, acts and decisions
of the Tree Board. Any person may appeal from any ruling or order of the Tree
Board to the City Council who may hear the matter and make a final decision.
(Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
TITLE 4
BUSINESS AND LICENSE REGULATIONS 1
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL LICENSE PROVISIONS
SECTION:
4-1-1: Administrative Provisions
4-1-2: Application For License
4-1-3: License Fee
4-1-4: Term Of License
4-1-5: Inspections
4-1-6: Interstate Commerce
4-1-7: Unlawful Activities Not Licensed
4-1-8: Licensed Property Subject To Lien
4-1-9: Revocation Or Denial Of License
4-1-10: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. MCA § 7-21-4101.
4-1-1: ADMINISTRATIVE PROVISIONS:
   A.   Collection; Application: The city clerk-treasurer shall be charged with
the collection of the licenses herein provided for, and application for
license, accompanied by a fee therefor, shall be filed with him. In his
discretion or in the discretion of the mayor, such applications may be held
until the next regular meeting of the city council following the application,
when it shall be submitted to the city council, who may decline to issue such
license, if, in the judgment of the city council, it will be for the best
interests of the city to refuse such license. Upon such refusal, the license
fee paid upon application shall be returned to the applicant. The city clerk-
treasurer shall prepare all blanks for applications and for licenses and books
of account in connection therewith, and all shall, so far as is possible, be
charged against the funds collected under this chapter, to be segregated and
deposited as hereinafter provided. All applications made and all licenses
issued under this chapter shall bear upon their face the following:
This application is made subject to all of the terms and conditions of Title 4,
Chapter 1 of the City Code of the City of Forsyth, which are hereby agreed to
and this license is not transferable.
   B.   Form Preparation; Filing: Forms for all licenses and permits, and
applications therefor, shall be prepared and kept on file by the city clerk-
treasurer.
   C.   Signature Of Officials: Each license or permit issued shall bear the
signature of the city clerk-treasurer in the absence of any provision to the
contrary. (Ord. 2000-04, 11-13-2000, eff. 12-13-2000)
4-1-2: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Applications for all licenses and permits required by this code shall be made
to the city clerk-treasurer, unless otherwise specified. The applicant shall
furnish such information as the city clerk-treasurer may require for
preparation of the license. (Ord. 2000-04, 11-13-2000, eff. 12-13-2000)
4-1-3: LICENSE FEE:
   A.   Required; Enumerated: Unless specifically exempted by state law, all
persons and/or entities doing business or engaged in commerce in the city,
whether residents or nonresidents, are required to pay city license fees.
Residents are required to pay an annual license fee of fifty dollars ($50.00).
Any person and/or entity with five (5) or more available rental units will be
considered a business.
      1.   Residents or nonresidents, considered to be itinerant vendors, that
intend to operate a temporary business for the sale of goods must obtain a
temporary business license and pay a fee of twenty five dollars ($25.00). A
temporary business is defined as one in which goods are sold on not more than
six (6) calendar days each year.
      2.   Nonprofit organizations, service clubs, public service organizations
are exempt from paying the license fee. (Ord. 2015-09, 12-21-2015)
   B.   Two Or More Businesses:
      1.   Separate Fee: In any case where any persons conduct, operate,
transact, engage in or carry on two (2) or more different lines of business,
industry, trade, pursuit, profession or vocation, under the same roof, they
shall pay only one license.
   C.   Distribution: It is hereby declared that all fees received by the city
for licenses under this chapter are to be allocated to the general fund for
administration and regulation of health and public safety for distribution by
city council action. (Ord. 2000-04, 11-13-2000, eff. 12-13-2000)
4-1-4: TERM OF LICENSE:
   A.   Specified: All licenses shall be payable in advance on or before
January 31 of each year and all licenses shall expire on December 31 of the
year of issuance.
   B.   Time Limit: The licenses herein provided for are for the calendar year
so long as this chapter stays in force and effect. (Ord. 2000-04, 11-13-2000,
eff. 12-13-2000)
4-1-5: INSPECTIONS:
Every person licensed under the provisions of this chapter shall be subject to
regulation, inspection, control and supervision under the general police power
of the city and of all of the provisions of this code now in force or which may
be adopted, in aid of such police power and regulation and each and every
license shall be subject to suspension and revocation as hereinafter provided.
(Ord. 2000-04, 11-13-2000, eff. 12-13-2000)
4-1-6: INTERSTATE COMMERCE:
Nothing in this chapter contained is intended to operate so as to interfere
with the power of the congress of the United States to regulate commerce
between the states, as such power is defined by the supreme court of the United
States. (Ord. 2000-04, 11-13-2000, eff. 12-13-2000)
4-1-7: UNLAWFUL ACTIVITIES NOT LICENSED:
No provision herein contained shall be construed as to license any trade,
business, occupation, pursuit, profession or entertainment prohibited by any
law of the United States, the state or by any provision of this code. (Ord.
2000-04, 11-13-2000, eff. 12-13-2000)
4-1-8: LICENSED PROPERTY SUBJECT TO LIEN 1 :
All property held or used in any trade, occupation, business, vocation, pursuit
or profession, for which a license is required by the provisions of this code,
is liable for such license and subject to a lien for the amount thereof, which
lien has precedence of any other lien, claim or demand, except liens, claims,
or other demands of the United States and the state, or of either of them; and
if any person fails or refuses to procure a license before the transaction of
the business specified, except as otherwise herein provided, the city clerk-
treasurer must seize such property or any other property belonging to such
person, association, firm or corporation, and sell the same in the manner
provided in section 15-17-911, Montana Code Annotated, and all acts amendatory
thereto. Such procedure for the collection of such license shall be cumulative
and in addition to any other procedure or penalty herein provided for violation
of this chapter. (Ord. 2000-04, 11-13-2000, eff. 12-13-2000)
 
Notes
1 1. MCA § 7-21-2104.
4-1-9: REVOCATION OR DENIAL OF LICENSE:
   A.   Failure To Comply; Unlawful Activities: Any license issued pursuant to
the provisions of this code or of any ordinance of the city may be revoked and
any application denied by the city council because of:
      1.   The failure of the licensee or applicant to comply with the
conditions and requirements of this code or any ordinance of the city.
      2.   Unlawful activities conducted or permitted on the premises where the
business is conducted.
   B.   Notice To Licensee: Prior to the revocation of a license, or denial of
an application to renew business license, the licensee or applicant shall be
given a notice which shall state in substance that the city council intends to
revoke the business license or deny the application to renew, together with the
reason or reasons therefor, at a regular or special meeting of the city council
(which shall be at least 10 days and not more than 30 days from the date notice
is sent), and that the licensee or applicant has a right to appear, to be
represented by counsel, to hear the evidence against him, to cross examine
witnesses and to present evidence as to why the license should not be revoked
or the application denied.
   C.   Not Applicable To Businesses Not Previously Licensed: The preceding
subsection shall not apply to applications for licenses for businesses which
have not previously been licensed by the city, and such applicants need only be
informed that their application has been denied. (Ord. 2000-04, 11-13-2000,
eff. 12-13-2000)
4-1-10: PENALTY:
Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as specified
in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 2
LIQUOR CONTROL 1
SECTION:
4-2-1: License Required
4-2-2: Fee For License
4-2-3: Inspections
4-2-4: State License
4-2-5: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. MCA § 16-1-101.
4-2-1: LICENSE REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of alcoholic
beverage sales without first procuring a license therefor from the city. (1999
Code)
4-2-2: FEE FOR LICENSE:
   A.   All-Beverage License:
      1.   Each holder of a Montana all-beverage license, owning and/or
operating under such license within the city limits, shall pay the city an
annual license fee of three hundred fifty dollars ($350.00). The annual fee
herein required shall be due and payable on January 2 of each year. (Ord. 2015-
04, 6-22-2015)
      2.   Provided, however, that where a license hereunder is issued for a
period commencing subsequent to the first of the current year for which such
license may be issued, a pro rata fee only shall be charged for the balance of
such current year, but nothing herein shall be construed to entitle any
licensee hereunder to any refund of any portion of the license fee in the event
of his discontinuing such business, or the suspension or revocation of his
license, prior to the expiration of such year, except and save that he shall be
entitled to a pro rata refund in the event that his business is discontinued by
virtue of said act being, by referendum petition, rendered inoperative awaiting
such time as it may be passed upon at an election, and the determination and
declaration of the result as provided by law.
      3.   The license fees herein provided for are exclusive of and in
addition to other license fees chargeable by the city for the sale of liquor,
beer and malt beverages, or any other licenses chargeable. (Ord. 190, 2-11-
1965; amd. Res., 11-4-1974)
   B.   Beer And Wine: Every person who offers for sale directly or indirectly,
for consumption on premises or off premises, dispenses beer or wine as
described and defined in the Montana Code Annotated within the city, must first
obtain a license for the sale thereof from the city clerk-treasurer, for which
said license such person must pay to the city clerk-treasurer, annually, in
advance, January 2 of each year, the following amounts: (Ord., 2-14-1983, eff.
3-17-1983; amd. 1999 Code)
      1.   Each beer only retailer, on premises consumption, two hundred fifty
dollars ($250.00).
      2.   Beer only retailer, on premises consumption, with wine license
amendment, an additional two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00).
      3.   Retail beer, for off premises consumption, either alone or in
conjunction with license to sell table wine for off premises consumption, two
hundred fifty dollars ($250.00). (Ord. 2015-04, 6-22-2015)
   C.   Refunds: Nothing herein shall be construed to entitle any licensee to a
refund of any portion of the license fee in the event of discontinuing his
business or suspension or revocation of his license. (Ord., 2-14-1983, eff. 3-
17-1983; amd. 1999 Code)
   D.   Disposition Of Fees: All receipts from license fees and fines collected
under the provisions of this chapter shall be deposited to the credit of the
general fund of the city, out of which said fund the cost of administering this
chapter shall be paid. (Ord. 157, 3-22-1937)
4-2-3: INSPECTIONS:
The city council or any duly authorized representative thereof, or the mayor,
shall have the right at any time to make an examination of the premises of such
licensee as to whether this chapter is being complied with. (Ord. 157, 3-22-
1937; amd. 1999 Code)
4-2-4: STATE LICENSE:
   A.   Required: No license provided for in this chapter may be issued until
the applicant has been issued a similar license by the State. (Ord., 2-14-1983,
eff. 3-17-1983)
   B.   Revocation Or Suspension: If any license issued by the State for retail
sales of alcoholic beverages, as provided for herein, shall be revoked or
suspended under the provisions of State law, the accompanying City license
issued hereunder shall automatically be revoked and suspended for the same
period. (Ord., eff. 2-15-1985)
4-2-5: PENALTY:
Except as otherwise provided by Montana law, violations of this chapter are
designated as Municipal infractions as specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this
Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)

4-3-1: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
Public conveyances shall be regulated in accordance with the rules, regulations
and requirements of the Public Service Commission. (1999 Code)

CHAPTER 5
CAMPGROUNDS AND TRAILER COURTS
SECTION:
4-5-1: Definitions
4-5-2: Applicability
4-5-3: Enforcement
4-5-4: Health Permit Required
4-5-5: Zoning Compliance
4-5-6: Alteration To Dwelling
4-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
CAMPGROUND: Any place, area or tract of land upon which is located any trailer,
trailer house, wagon, tent or tent house used for camping purposes or living
quarters.
TRAILER, CAMP CAR, TRAILER HOUSE: Any unit used for living or sleeping
purposes, which is equipped with wheels or similar devices and used for the
purpose of transporting said unit from place to place, whether by motive power
or other means, also such vehicles as are used as aforesaid that have had the
wheels or equipment removed. (Ord. 164, 6-7-1950)
4-5-2: APPLICABILITY:
The provisions of this chapter shall be applicable to every campground within
the corporate area of the City and it shall be unlawful for any person to
maintain, operate, conduct or carry on such campground, or for any person
living or sleeping in any camp car or trailer located in a campground, or for
any other person to violate or to contribute in any way to the violation of any
of the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 164, 6-7-1950)
4-5-3: ENFORCEMENT:
It shall be the duty of the City to enforce all of the regulations of this
chapter and for the purpose of securing enforcement thereof, the County
Sanitation Officer, or any of his duly authorized representatives, or the
building inspector, shall have the right and are hereby empowered to enter upon
the premises of any campground now operating or which may hereafter be operated
within the City, to inspect the same and all accommodations connected
therewith. Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions
as specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018,
eff. 1-1-2019)
4-5-4: HEALTH PERMIT REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or maintain or to offer for
public use within the confines of the City as hereinafter set forth, any
campgrounds without applying for and receiving from the County Sanitation
Officer a health permit, or without complying with the regulations set forth
and any rules and regulations which may be formulated by the County Sanitation
Officer, from time to time, and the laws of the State. (Ord. 164, 6-7-1950;
amd. 1999 Code)
4-5-5: ZONING COMPLIANCE:
   A.   Location Of Campgrounds: Campgrounds hereinafter established shall be
located in accordance with the provisions of the zoning regulations. (Ord. 164,
6-7-1950; amd. 1999 Code)
   B.   Mobile Home Courts; Arrangement And Spacing: Lots in mobile home courts
shall conform to the requirements set forth in the current code as adopted.
(Ord. 2015-05, 6-22-2015)
4-5-6: ALTERATION TO DWELLING:
It shall be unlawful for any person owning or operating a camp car or trailer
located in a campground to remove or cause to be removed the wheels or any
similar transportation device from said camp car or trailer, or to otherwise
permanently affix it to the ground in a manner that would prevent the ready
removal of said camp car or trailer, without first obtaining a permit so to do
from the building inspector. Any alteration of any camp car or trailer or
trailer house, as above set forth, shall be construed as removing it from the
requirements of this chapter and converting it into a dwelling, and it shall
thereupon be subject to the requirements of the Building Code 1 . (Ord. 164, 6-
7-1950)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 11 of this Code.
CHAPTER 6
AFTER HOURS CARD GAMES
SECTION:
4-6-1: Live Card Games Authorized
4-6-2: Live Card Game Act
4-6-3: Permit Required
4-6-4: Compliance With Montana Law
4-6-5: Video Gaming Machine Operation Not Authorized
4-6-6: Violation Of Chapter
4-6-1: LIVE CARD GAMES AUTHORIZED:
The City of Forsyth hereby authorizes the operation of live card games between
the hours of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. and eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. for each day
for facilities with an alcoholic beverage license. This time is in addition to
the time allowed under State law for the operation of live card games between
eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. and two o'clock (2:00) A.M. (Ord. 2008-02, 10-27-
2008, eff. 11-27-2008)
4-6-2: LIVE CARD GAME ACT:
This chapter authorizes the operation of any live card game, which is under the
Live Card Game Act under Montana Code Annotated section 23-5-311. (Ord. 2008-
02, 10-27-2008, eff. 11-27-2008)
4-6-3: PERMIT REQUIRED:
Any establishment, which operates a live card game between the hours of two
o'clock (2:00) A.M. and eight o'clock (8:00) A.M., must submit a permit
application to the City. The permit application is available at the City
Clerk's Office. Approval of the permit will be obtained by the Forsyth City
Council. No fee for the permit is required. (Ord. 2008-02, 10-27-2008, eff. 11-
27-2008)
4-6-4: COMPLIANCE WITH MONTANA LAW:
In order to maintain the permit, any establishment conducting the live card
game from two o'clock (2:00) A.M. to eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. must comply with
all applicable rules and regulations for operation of an after hours live card
game and the related facility as established by the State of Montana. (Ord.
2008-02, 10-27-2008, eff. 11-27-2008)
4-6-5: VIDEO GAMING MACHINE OPERATION NOT AUTHORIZED:
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to authorize the operation of video
gaming machines between the hours of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. and eight o'clock
(8:00) A.M. (Ord. 2008-02, 10-27-2008, eff. 11-27-2008)
4-6-6: VIOLATION OF CHAPTER:
Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as specified
in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
TITLE 5
PUBLIC HEALTH AND SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
NUISANCES
ARTICLE A. REFUSE IN BUILDINGS; STAGNANT WATER
SECTION:
5-1A-1: Nuisance Declared
5-1A-2: Enforcement
5-1A-3: Penalty
5-1A-1: NUISANCE DECLARED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or suffer to be in or accumulate
in or upon any yard, lot, place or premises or upon any street or sidewalk
adjacent to or abutting upon any lot, block, place or premises or in any
building or shed owned or occupied by him or for which he may be an agent
within the limits of the City, any stagnant water or impure water, refuse,
vegetable decay or decaying substance, garbage or filth of any kind, nor suffer
such yard, lot, place, building or premises to be or to remain in such
condition as to cause or create a nuisance or offensive smell or to pollute or
render unhealthful the atmosphere or the premises or thereby to be, become,
cause or create a public nuisance. (1961 Code §
8-5-1)
5-1A-2: ENFORCEMENT:
The provisions of this article shall be enforced as provided in Montana Code
Annotated section 7-5-4104. (1999 Code)
5-1A-3: PENALTY:
Violations of this article are designated as Municipal infractions as specified
in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 2
ABANDONED CONTAINERS
SECTION:
5-2-1: Refrigerators
5-2-1: REFRIGERATORS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to leave or permit to remain outside of any
dwelling, building or other structure or within any unoccupied or abandoned
building, structure or dwelling under his control, in a place accessible to
children, any abandoned, unattended or discarded refrigerator, freezer, or
other container which has a door or lid, snaplock or other locking device which
may not be released from the inside, without first removing said door or lid,
snaplock or other locking device. Violations of this chapter are designated as
Municipal infractions as specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord.
2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 3
GARBAGE AND REFUSE 1
SECTION:
5-3-1: Defined
5-3-2: Disposal Of Garbage
5-3-3: Collection Times
5-3-4: Trucks For Collection
5-3-5: Duty Of Owner Or Occupant
5-3-6: Apartments
5-3-7: Containers
5-3-8: Rates And Refunds
5-3-9: Financial Administration
5-3-10: Rules And Regulations
5-3-11: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. MCA § 7-14-4105.
5-3-1: DEFINED:
   A.   The word "garbage", as used in this chapter, is intended to mean all
refuse, animal and vegetable matter, ashes, store sweepings, paper and rubbish,
and other waste matter, but shall not be construed to mean or include manure.
(Ord. 159, 1-7-1943)
   B.   Garbage does not include waste products from building or other
construction operations, such as lime, plaster, sand, concrete, hard steel,
large appliances, nor other refuse. (Eff. 11-9-1978)
5-3-2: DISPOSAL OF GARBAGE:
   A.   Facility: All garbage must be conveyed to the solid waste disposal unit
(compactor) located immediately west of Highway 12 and the west intersection of
Main Street, and must be transported to that location either by city garbage
trucks or by individual citizens of the city, during those hours when the
facility is open, as posted thereon.
   B.   Administration: The collection, removal and disposal of garbage shall
be done and performed under the supervision, direction and control of the
director of public works and the city council, subject to such rules and
regulations as may be made from time to time by the city council. (10-26-1981)
   C.   Private Removal: For the purpose of this chapter, nothing herein shall
prevent the city council from permitting or requiring the owner or occupant of
a premises to remove the garbage therefrom at his own expense under the
supervision and control of the public works director and exempting said
premises from taxation hereunder. (Ord. 95-03, 7-10-1995)
5-3-3: COLLECTION TIMES:
The city shall provide for domestic and commercial garbage collections at such
time or times as the city council may hereinafter direct. (10-26-1981)
5-3-4: TRUCKS FOR COLLECTION:
It shall be optional with the city council whether the city shall own and
supply to said collectors trucks used in the collection and removal of garbage,
or require the same to be furnished by said collectors. All garbage trucks
shall be of such style, size and description as the city council may from time
to time require and shall bear in prominent letters the words "City of
Forsyth". (Ord. 159, 1-7-1943; amd. Ord. 98-01, 5-26-1998, eff. 6-26-1998)
5-3-5: DUTY OF OWNER OR OCCUPANT:
It shall be the duty of the owner or occupant of any premises within the city
limits to keep such premises and one-half (1/2) of the street and alley or
avenue immediately adjacent thereto, and also the gutter in front of or
adjoining his property clean (and shall fill with gravel layer and shall keep
weed free), open and free from any ashes, offal, wastepapers, cans, glass,
broken ware, dirt, rubbish, filth, yard cleanings, garbage, barnyard litter or
any unhealthful stuff or material of any sort or kind. (Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-
2015)
5-3-6: APARTMENTS:
   For the purpose of this chapter, two (2) or more rooms occupied together
shall constitute an apartment, and nothing herein shall prevent the city
council from permitting or requiring the owner or occupant of the premises to
remove the garbage therefrom at his own expense under the supervision and
control of the Code Enforcement Officer, and exempting said premises from
taxation hereunder.
(Ord. 159, 1-7-1943; amd. Ord. 98-01, 5-26-1998, eff. 6-26-1998; Ord. 2024-02,
12-16-2024)
5-3-7: CONTAINERS:
   A.   Supply; Classifications: It shall be optional with the City Council
whether the City shall own and supply to said collectors containers for holding
garbage used in the collection and removal of garbage, or require the same to
be furnished by said collectors. All containers shall be of such style, size
and description as the City Council may from time to time require, and shall
bear in prominent letters the words “City of Forsyth” and shall be of the
following volume classifications:
      1.   Ninety five (95) gallon roll-out refuse container;
      2.   Three hundred (300) gallon refuse container.
   B.   Sharing: Sharing of containers is limited to three (3) users; requests
must be made in writing at City Hall; each user will be assessed separately.
   C.   Failure To Comply: Recipients of garbage service failing to comply with
proper directives from the Code Enforcement Officer or the City Council as to
the placement of garbage cans, rules and restrictions governing placement of
restricted materials in containers, open lids and overflow of garbage from
containers may be denied service until such time as they comply.
   D.   Placement On Sidewalks: Properties serviced by curbside pickup shall
not have containers on sidewalks, except for day of scheduled pickup.
(Ord. 98-01, 5-26-1998, eff. 6-26-1998; amd. Ord. 2024-02, 12-16-2024)
5-3-8: RATES AND REFUNDS:
   A.   Filed With City Clerk-Treasurer: The garbage collection fee for each
fiscal year shall be on file in the City Clerk- Treasurer's office. (Ord. 97-
03, 7-18-1997)
   B.   Vacant Property: Property that is vacant shall not be assessed a
garbage collection fee. The garbage ratepayer must furnish the City with a
services discontinuance notice at the commencement of the vacancy. Property so
listed for one year will be removed from the garbage assessment rolls at the
time of garbage assessment review, as specified in subsection 5-3-9C2 of this
Chapter. (Ord. 97-03, 7-18-1997; amd. Ord. 98-01, 5-26-1998, eff. 6-26-1998)
   C.   Succeeding Years: Garbage taxation for succeeding years will be
assessed by the City Council annually upon recommendation of City officers and
levied against real property within the City. Said assessment shall be lawful
and reasonable considering service rendered by the City and usage by property
owners. The annual rates may be set by resolution.
   D.   New Or Increased Service: Owner/occupants of property requiring new or
increased garbage service during the year will be billed by the City Clerk-
Treasurer for the prorated service cost for the remainder of the year.
   E.   Temporary Service: Requests for temporary, nonrecurring increases in
service will be billed by the City Clerk- Treasurer for the prorated monthly
service cost for the months service is requested. (Ord. 97-03, 7-18-1997)
5-3-9: FINANCIAL ADMINISTRATION:
   A.   Garbage Fund: The expense of collecting, removal and disposition of
garbage shall be paid for out of the Garbage Fund of the City. The cost of
collecting garbage, exclusive of manure, from the streets, alleys and private
premises of the City shall in all cases be assessed and taxed against the real
estate from which such garbage is deposited, and such property owner shall, as
far as practicable, bear its share of the expense of collecting and disposing
of the garbage in proportion to the amount of garbage deposited therefrom.
(Ord. 159, 1-7-1943)
   B.   Tax List:
      1.   Preparation; Contents: The Public Works Director shall prepare a
list of all lots or parts of lots in the City upon which there are buildings or
other improvements or cultivation necessitating the removal of garbage. Such
lists shall show in connection with each lot the nature of the type, style or
size of the container. Said list shall also show the number of containers
necessary for fixing the rate of taxation hereinafter set forth. Such list
shall be filed with the City Clerk-Treasurer and constitute the list of lots
upon which Garbage Taxes shall be collected each year.
      2.   It shall be the duty of the Public Works Director each year on and
before April 1, to report to the City Clerk-Treasurer a list of all lots or
fractions of lots in the City not heretofore taxed, upon which buildings or
improvements have been erected or constructed or cultivation done necessitating
the removal of garbage since the last assessment, and any addition to
buildings, which shall effect the rate of taxation as hereinafter set forth,
and the City Clerk-Treasurer shall make the necessary additions and changes in
the list of lots liable for Garbage Taxes on file in his office. (Ord. 95-03,
7-10-1995; amd. Ord. 98-01, 5-26-1998, eff. 6-26-1998)
   C.   Extended Tax Assessment List:
      1.   Assessment: It shall be the duty of the City Clerk- Treasurer each
year immediately after the passage of the resolution fixing the basic Garbage
Taxes for the year shall have been introduced, to extend on the list of lots
liable for the tax, the total amount to be taxed against each lot or portion of
a lot under the provisions of this chapter, and at least twenty one (21) days
before the date set for final adoption, to publish in the official newspaper of
the City, a notice to all lot owners of the passage of said resolution, and
time and place, when and where the said list is on file in the City Clerk-
Treasurer's Office for inspection. Any person having any objections to offer,
wherefore, said tax should not be levied and collected, shall file the same
with the City Clerk-Treasurer not more than fifteen (15) days from the date of
said notice. At the time of said publication, the City Clerk-Treasurer also
shall mail a copy of the proposed garbage assessment to all lot owners whose
assessment therefore has been increased from the assessment levied in the
preceding year, except in the case of general rate increases. (Ord. 97-03, 6-
18-1997; amd. 1999 Code)
      2.   Objections: At the next regular meeting of the City Council, after
the expiration of the notice to lot owners prescribed in subsection C1 of this
section, the City Council shall pass upon all objections filed and make such
changes in the assessment as it shall find necessary and proper after hearing
such objections and thereafter, the City Clerk- Treasurer shall incorporate
such changes in the list of taxes as extended by him and thereafter shall
certify the taxes on such amended list, to be by him collected in the same
manner as other special taxes and assessments. (Ord. 159, 1-7-1943; amd. 1999
Code)
5-3-10: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
   A.   Authority: The City Council may make such other rules and regulations
concerning the depositing, handling, removing, and disposition of garbage as
they may from time to time deem fit and proper.
   B.   Unapproved Items; Ash: Items not allowed in containers include carpet,
wood, branches and tree limbs, rocks and ash. Ash must be hauled to the
transfer station by the property owner.
   C.   Unauthorized Disposal: It shall be unlawful for any person to knowingly
dump, dispose or otherwise transfer garbage in their possession into a City
garbage container located on the property of another owner, tenant or
government entity without their expressed permission. Violations of this
chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as specified in title 1,
chapter 4 of this Code.
(Ord. 159, 1-7-1943; amd. Ord. 98-01, 5-26-1998, eff. 6-26-1998; 1999 Code;
Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019; amd. Ord. 2024-02, 12-16-2024)
5-3-11: PENALTY:
Any individual or legal entity failing to comply with the requirements of this
chapter may be denied City garbage service until such time as they comply.
Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as specified
in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 4
WEED CONTROL
SECTION:
5-4-1: Enforcement
5-4-2: Destruction Or Removal Of Weeds
5-4-3: Continuing Notice
5-4-1: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Duty Of Enforcement Officer: It shall be the duty of the Code
Enforcement Officer or the Public Works Director to enforce the provisions of
this chapter and for the purpose of enforcement, shall make frequent
inspections of all of the lots and tracts of land within the city. Should the
owner or occupant neglect or refuse to comply with the provisions of this
chapter, the Code Enforcement Officer or the Public Works Director shall cause
such necessary work to be done as may be deemed necessary, when directed to do
so by the city council, cause an itemized bill of the expense to be files with
the city clerk/treasurer, who will certify to same and collect such costs in
the manner of other city taxes.
   B.   Nonpayment Of Property Assessments: Anytime the City is required,
either through their employees, or to a contractor to resolve, remedy, or
otherwise abate a condition in which the property owner is in violation of the
City, the owner is billed for such repair, and the owner does not pay the bill
within sixty (60) calendar days of the notice, failure to pay will be
considered nonpayment. Nonpayment shall be a considered lien against the
property, and is enforceable in the same manner as nonpayment of Property Taxes
is enforced.
   In the event the property owner who is billed objects or challenges to the
amount of the bill, or any other issues related to the bill, they may request
to be placed upon the agenda at a regularly scheduled City Council meeting at
any time before the expiration of the sixty (60) day period.
   C.   Posting Of Weed Control Notice: The city council designee will post a
Weed Control Notice, which summarizes the provisions of Chapter 4, Weed
Control. The notices will be posted at Forsyth City Hall, Forsyth Post Office
and Rosebud County Courthouse. The notice will be printed in the Independent
Press on two (2) consecutive weeks. All notices will be posted prior to March
15 of each year.
(Ord. 113, 6-3-1920; amd. Ord. 98-05, eff. 12-24-1998; Ord. 2001-02, 12-27-
2001, eff. 1-27-2002; Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015; Ord. 2022-08, 1-16-2023; Ord.
2024-03, 12-16-2024)
5-4-2: DESTRUCTION OR REMOVAL OF WEEDS:
   A.   Required; Weeds Specified: Pursuant to the authority as provided by
Montana Code Annotated section 7-22-4101, owners of all lots or parcels of land
within the City limits, shall cause to be cut, destroyed or removed (not
limited to) all dandelions, fan weed, fireweed, thistles, noxious weeds, grass
and all other nonornamental vegetation over twelve inches (12") in height
growing on their property (includes alleys and streets). Such owners shall be
responsible for removal of those weeds after receiving reasonable notice given
by either the Code Enforcement Officer, Public Works Director or other
authorized employee of the City or County.
   B.   Failure To Comply; Assessment And Penalty: The City may levy the cost
of weed extermination and removal and may bill or otherwise assess such cost as
a special tax against the property in the event the landowner fails to
satisfactorily remove the weeds within a reasonable time after notice.
Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as specified
in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code.
   C.   Public Nuisance; Additional Sanction: In addition, failure to
satisfactorily remove the weeds, within a reasonable time after notice, (Title
5-11-3) may be considered the maintenance of a public nuisance in violation of
Montana Code Annotated section 45-8-11, and the offender will be subject to
additional sanction as provided under law.
   D.   Any vegetation (trees, hedges, bushes, grasses, weeds, etc.)
originating from individual properties that extrude into city right of way on
any sidewalk, street or alley shall be the responsibility of that property
owner to remediate when given reasonable notice (5-11-3) by the Code
Enforcement Officer, Public Works Director or other city employee tasked with
enforcement.
   Remediation would include trimming or removing of offending vegetation to
the property line, or further into the property to prevent future encroachment.
(Ord. 97-08, 11-24-1997, eff. 12-26-1997; amd. Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015; Ord.
2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019; Ord. 2024-03, 12-16-2024)
5-4-3: CONTINUING NOTICE:
   A notice issued of this chapter shall be deemed a continuing notice
regarding the weeds or other vegetation described in the notice for a period of
one year from the date of service and is valid for all locations within the
City of Forsyth, Montana. No further notice by an Enforcement Officer or ten
(10) day period to abate is necessary to abate a nuisance created by said
vegetation within the one-year period.
   This change shall become effective thirty (30) days after date of second
reading and passage by the City Council as required by law.
(Ord. 2024-03, 12-16-2024)
CHAPTER 5
TREES 1
SECTION:
5-5-1: Short Title
5-5-2: Definitions
5-5-3: Separability
5-5-4: Street Tree Species List
5-5-5: Spacing
5-5-6: Distance From Curb And Sidewalk
5-5-7: Distance From Street Corners And Fireplugs
5-5-8: Utilities
5-5-9: Public Tree Care
5-5-10: Trimming; Corner Clearance
5-5-11: Tree Topping
5-5-12: Abuse Or Mutilation Of Public Trees
5-5-13: Hedges
5-5-14: Dead Or Diseased Trees; Pruning, Removal
5-5-15: Pruning Or Removal Procedures
5-5-16: Interference With Tree Board Or Agent
5-5-17: Arborist License And Insurance
5-5-18: Tree, Shrub, Hedge, Etc. Encroachment On City Right Of Way
5-5-19: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 3, chapter 2 of this code.
5-5-1: SHORT TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the MUNICIPAL TREE ORDINANCE OF
THE CITY OF FORSYTH, FORSYTH, MONTANA. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms, phrases, words, and their
derivations shall have the meanings given herein. When not inconsistent with
the context, words used in the present tense include the future, words in the
plural include the singular and words in the singular include the plural. The
word shall is mandatory and not merely directory.
AGENT: Any person or persons specifically authorized by the city tree board
including the mayor and public works director to carry out its activities and
functions.
BOULEVARD: The "boulevard" or "parking" shall mean the space between the
sidewalk, or the normal location of the sidewalk and the curb line or curb.
LARGE TREES: Those attaining a height of forty five feet (45') or more at
maturity.
MEDIUM TREES: Those attaining a height of thirty (30) to forty five feet (45')
at maturity.
MUNICIPALITY: The city, town, village, subdivision, or otherwise designated
area unit of the city of Forsyth, Rosebud County, Montana.
PARK TREE: Trees, shrubs, bushes and all other woody vegetation in public parks
having individual names, and all areas owned by the city, or to which the
public has free access as a park.
PARKWAYS: Linear public lands not formally designated as parks.
PROPERTY OWNER OR OWNER: The person owning such property as shown by the county
treasurer of Rosebud County, state of Montana.
PUBLIC TREES: Shall include all shade and ornamental trees now or hereafter
growing on any street or any public place where otherwise indicated.
SMALL TREES: Those attaining a height of twenty (20) to thirty feet (30') at
maturity.
STREET TREES: Trees, shrubs, bushes, and all other woody vegetation on land
lying between property lines on either side of all streets, avenues, or ways
within the city.
TREES: All shade and ornamental trees and all shrubs and other beautification
or landscape plantings, now or hereafter planted or growing within the
Municipality. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005; amd. Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015)
5-5-3: SEPARABILITY:
Should any part or provision of this chapter be declared by a court of
competent jurisdiction to be invalid, the same shall not affect the validity of
this chapter as a whole, or any part thereof, other than the part declared
invalid. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-4: STREET TREE SPECIES LIST:
The Tree Board shall maintain a list of approved and not allowed trees for use
in public rights-of-way. The list will be on file and available at City Hall.
Said list shall constitute the requirements of the City and shall be open to
review. (Ord. 2018-04, 12-10-2018)
5-5-5: SPACING:
The spacing of street trees will be in accordance with the three (3) tree size
classes listed in section
5-5-2, "Definitions", of this chapter, and no trees may be planted closer
together than the following: small trees, twenty feet (20'); medium trees,
thirty feet (30'); and large trees, forty feet (40'). (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-
2005)
5-5-6: DISTANCE FROM CURB AND SIDEWALK:
The distance trees may be planted from curbs or curb lines and sidewalks will
be in accordance with the three (3) tree size classes listed in section
5-5-2, "Definitions", of this chapter, and no trees may be planted closer to
any curb or sidewalk than the following: small trees, two feet (2'); medium
trees, three feet (3'); and large trees, four feet (4'); with the exception of
trees in the downtown tree program (sidewalks), one foot (1') from the curb.
(Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-7: DISTANCE FROM STREET CORNERS AND FIREPLUGS:
Tree planting shall conform to the City of Forsyth's clear vision ordinance in
regard to street corners and alleyways. No tree shall be planted closer than
ten feet (10') of any fireplug. Owners of existing plantings violating this
rule must keep them carefully pruned and trimmed to obviate their creating a
vision obstruction of vehicle drivers, unless they be declared a nuisance and
compulsorily removed. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-8: UTILITIES:
No street trees other than species falling in the small tree class of section
5-5-2, "Definitions", of this chapter may be planted under or within ten (10)
lateral feet of any overhead utility wire, or over or within five (5) lateral
feet of any underground water line, sewer line, transmission line or other
utility. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-9: PUBLIC TREE CARE:
The City shall have the right to plant, prune, maintain and remove trees,
plants and shrubs within the lines of all streets, alleys, avenues, lanes,
squares and public grounds, as may be necessary to ensure public safety or to
preserve or enhance the symmetry and beauty of such public grounds. (Ord. 2005-
03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-10: TRIMMING; CORNER CLEARANCE:
It shall be the duty of any person or persons owning or occupying real property
bordering on any street upon which property there may be trees, to prune such
trees in such manner that they will not obstruct or shade the streetlights,
obstruct the passage of pedestrians on sidewalks, obstruct vision of traffic
signs, or obstruct view of any street or alley intersections. The minimum
clearance of any overhanging portion thereof shall be eight feet (8') over
sidewalks, and twelve feet (12') over all streets except truck thoroughfares,
which shall have a clearance of sixteen feet (16'). (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-11: TREE TOPPING:
It shall be unlawful as a normal practice for any person, firm, or City
department to top any street tree, park tree, or other tree on public property.
"Topping" is defined as the severe cutting back of limbs to stubs larger than
three inches (3") in diameter within the tree's crown to such a degree so as to
remove the normal canopy and disfigure the tree. Trees severely damaged by
storms or other causes, or certain trees under utility wires or other
obstructions, where other pruning practices are impractical may be exempted
from this section at the determination of the City. Standards for all pruning
activities will, at minimum, be the National Arborist Association "Tree Pruning
Standards". (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-12: ABUSE OR MUTILATION OF PUBLIC TREES:
Unless specifically authorized by the City Tree Board, or its agent, no person
shall intentionally damage, cut, carve, transplant, or remove any public tree;
attach any rope, wire, nails, advertising posters or other contrivance to any
public tree; allow any gaseous liquid, or solid substance which is harmful to
such public trees to come in contact with them; or set fire or permit any fire
to burn when such fire or the heat thereof will injure any part of any public
tree. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-13: HEDGES:
Hedges along the street property line shall not be planted within two feet (2')
of the adjacent property line. The height and clear vision zones shall be in
conformity with the City of Forsyth's fence regulations. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-
2005)
5-5-14: DEAD OR DISEASED TREES; PRUNING, REMOVAL:
All trees and shrubs within the Municipality shall be pruned or removed when
such trees or shrubs constitute a hazard to life and property, or harbor
insects or disease, which constitute a threat to other trees or shrubs within
the City.
The Municipality may further remove or cause to be removed any tree or part
thereof which is in an unsafe condition or which by reason of its nature is
injurious to sewers, electric power lines, gas lines, water lines, or other
public improvements or is infected with an injurious fungus, insect or pest.
(Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-15: PRUNING OR REMOVAL PROCEDURES:
   A.   Notice To Prune Or Remove: For any person or persons owning real
property bordering any street who fails to prune or remove a tree in violation
of either section
5-5-10 or
5-5-14 of this chapter, the City shall order such a person or persons within
ten (10) days after written receipt or written notice to prune or remove such
trees. The order may be served by personal service, certified mail or
publication.
   B.   Hearing: In the event the property owner disagrees with the order, the
property owner may request a hearing before the City Council of Forsyth. Such
written request for hearing must be filed within fifteen (15) days from the
receipt of the order. This provision should not be construed to limit the
liability of the property owner that may be incurred for maintaining a
dangerous or diseased tree. This hearing should be held at the first Council
meeting, after the request, allowing for sufficient time for the matter to be
placed on the agenda.
   C.   Failure To Comply: When a person to whom an order is directed shall
fail to comply within the specified time, it shall be lawful for the City to
prune or remove such tree, and the exact cost thereof shall be assessed to the
owner as provided for by law in the case of special assessments. (Ord. 2005-03,
11-14-2005)
5-5-16: INTERFERENCE WITH TREE BOARD OR AGENT:
No person shall hinder, prevent, delay, or interfere with the Tree Board, or
its agent, while engaged in carrying out the execution or enforcement of this
chapter; provided, however, that nothing herein shall be construed as an
attempt to prohibit the pursuit of any remedy, legal or equitable, in any court
of competent jurisdiction of the protection of property rights by the owner of
any property within the Municipality. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-14-2005)
5-5-17: ARBORIST LICENSE AND INSURANCE:
It shall be unlawful for any person or firm to engage in the business or
occupation of trimming, pruning, treating, or removing trees within the City
without first applying for and procuring a business license.
Before any business license shall be issued, each applicant shall first file
evidence of current possession of liability insurance and current possession of
acceptable workers' compensation insurance as set by this Code.
Further, all applicants shall receive a copy of the applicable National
Arborist Association (NAA) "Tree Pruning Standards". These standards shall be
considered minimum requirements for lawful work within the City.
Current International Society of Arboriculture arborist certification may be
used as a criteria in awarding licenses or in contracting. (Ord. 2005-03, 11-
14-2005)
5-5-18: TREE, SHRUB, HEDGE, ETC. ENCROACHMENT ON CITY RIGHT OF WAY:
   A.   Any vegetation (trees, hedges, bushes, grasses, weeds, etc.)
originating from individual properties that extrude into city right of way on
any sidewalk, street or alley, shall be the responsibility of that property
owner to remediate when given reasonable notice (
5-11-3) by the Code Enforcement Officer, 5 Public Works Director or other city
employee tasked with enforcement.
   B.   Remediation would include trimming or removing of offending vegetation
to the property line or further into the property to prevent future
encroachment.
(Ord. 2024-04, 12-16-2024)
5-5-19: PENALTY:
   Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as
specified in
title 1, chapter 4 of this Code.
(Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 6
ANIMAL WASTES
SECTION:
5-6-1: Removal Required
5-6-2: Placement With Garbage Prohibited (Rep. by Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015)
5-6-3: Objection By Adjacent Inhabitants
5-6-4: Failure To Comply; Removal By City
5-6-5: Continuing Notice
5-6-1: REMOVAL REQUIRED:
   Every person owning or having control of one or more of the following kinds
of domestic animals: cats, dogs, and birds; birds does not mean barnyard fowl,
and keeping such animals within the City, shall keep the premises upon which
such animals are kept free from accumulations of manure, and shall remove such
manure from said premises at least twice during each calendar month, and
dispose of properly or more often, if required to do so by the Code Enforcement
Officer or Director of Public Works; and said Code Enforcement Officer or
Director of Public Works is hereby empowered to order removal of manure more
often than twice in any calendar month by the owner of property on which it may
accumulate whenever in the judgment of the Code Enforcement Officer or Director
of Public Works, the removal thereof is for any reason desirable.
(Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015; amd. Ord. 2024-05, 12-16-2024)
5-6-2: PLACEMENT WITH GARBAGE PROHIBITED:
(Rep. by Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015)
5-6-3: OBJECTION BY ADJACENT INHABITANTS:
No person owning or having control over one or more of the kinds of domestic
animals described in section
5-6-1 of this chapter shall keep such animals within the City limits when
seventy five percent (75%) of the adult inhabitants in the immediate
neighborhood object to the maintenance of such domestic animals within the City
limits; provided however, that such objection must be in writing, signed by at
least seventy five percent (75%) of the adult inhabitants within a radius of
three hundred feet (300') of the premises where such animals are being kept or
maintained. Said written objection shall be directed to the City Council. When
any such written objection is received by the City Council, the City Council
shall cause notice to be given to such person maintaining such animals within
the City limits. Upon receipt of such notice, such person shall forthwith
remove or cause to be removed, such domestic animals from such premises and
will not again use said premises for keeping or maintaining such animals,
unless at least seventy five percent (75%) of the adult inhabitants of the said
immediate neighborhood consent to such use. It shall be unlawful for any such
person to neglect, fail or refuse to remove such domestic animals after receipt
of said notice as herein provided or to again use said premises for such
purposes without said consent. (Res., eff. 9-22-1977)
5-6-4: FAILURE TO COMPLY; REMOVAL BY CITY:
   Should any person neglect or refuse to remove accumulations of manure from
private premises after being ordered to do so by an officer of the City as
provided in this chapter, the Code Enforcement Officer or Public Works Director
shall cause the same to be removed and shall certify the cost thereof to the
City Council. The City Council shall thereafter, by resolution, levy and assess
the cost thereof against the property from which said manure was so removed,
and the City Clerk-Treasurer shall transmit to the County Clerk a certified
copy of such resolution. In addition, violations of this chapter are designated
as Municipal infractions as specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code.
(Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019; amd. Ord. 2024-05, 12-16-2024)
5-6-5: CONTINUING NOTICE:
   A notice issued of this chapter shall be deemed a continuing notice
regarding the animal wastes described in the notice for a period of one year
from the date of service and is valid for all locations within the City of
Forsyth, Montana. No further notice by an Enforcement Officer or ten (10) day
period to abate is necessary to abate a nuisance created by said animal wastes
within the one-year period.
(Ord. 2024-05, 12-16-2024)
CHAPTER 7
ABANDONED AND JUNK VEHICLES, MACHINERY, TRAILERS AND PARTS 1
SECTION:
5-7-1: Purpose
5-7-2: Definitions
5-7-3: Exemptions
5-7-4: Junk Vehicle Deemed Nuisance
5-7-5: Administration And Enforcement
5-7-6: Administration Costs
5-7-7: Notices
5-7-8: Abatement And Removal
5-7-9: Illegal Off Street Parking
5-7-10: Continuing Notice
5-7-11: Penalty
5-7-12: Nonexclusive Of This Chapter
 
Notes
1 1. See title 7, chapter 6 of this code.
5-7-1: PURPOSE:
The city council of the city of Forsyth, Montana, hereby makes, finds and
declares that the accumulation and storage of abandoned, wrecked, dismantled,
or inoperative vehicles, machinery, trailers, or parts thereof, on public
property or illegally parked on private property is hereby found to create a
condition tending to reduce the value of private property, to promote blight
and deterioration, to invite plundering, to create fire hazards, to constitute
an attractive nuisance creating a hazard to the health and safety of minors, to
create a harbor for rodents and insects, and to be injurious to the health,
safety and general welfare. Therefore, the presence of an abandoned, dismantled
or inoperative vehicle, or part thereof, on public property or illegally parked
on private property, except as expressly hereinafter permitted, is hereby
declared to constitute a public nuisance, which may be abated as such in
accordance with the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 2003-05, 7-14-2003, eff.
8-14-2003)
5-7-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter the following definitions shall apply:
ABANDONED VEHICLE: Any of the following. For the purposes of this definition,
the word "vehicle" includes a vehicle, machinery, trailer or parts thereof:
   A.   A vehicle that has been left unattended on public property for more
than forty eight (48) hours and lacks current registration, plates, or one or
more wheels/tires or other parts which renders the vehicle totally inoperable;
   B.   A vehicle that has remained illegally parked on public property for
more than forty eight (48) hours;
   C.   A vehicle that has been unlawfully parked on private real property or
has been placed on private property without the consent of the real property
owner or person in control of the property for more than forty eight (48)
hours;
   D.   A vehicle that has been legally impounded by order of a law enforcement
authority and has not been reclaimed for a period of five (5) days. However, a
law enforcement authority may declare the vehicle abandoned within the five (5)
day period by commencing the notification process in Montana Code Annotated
title 61 chapter 8 (2001);
   E.   Any vehicle parked on a street determined by a law enforcement
authority to create a hazard to other vehicle traffic.
   F.   No vehicle shall be parked or left standing upon the right of way of
any public highway for a period longer than forty eight (48) hours, or upon a
city street, any state, county or city property for a period longer than five
(5) days. Montana code number 61.8.356.
ENFORCEMENT AUTHORITY: A peace officer or any city, state or federal department
or agency operating with arrest authority in Forsyth, Montana, or city council
designee.
JUNK VEHICLE: Any vehicle, machinery, trailer, or parts thereof, located on
public property or illegally parked on private property within the corporate
limits of the city of Forsyth, Montana, which, as to a vehicle or trailer, does
not properly display license plates or stickers indicating current registration
and/or, as to any vehicle, machinery, trailer, or parts thereof, which has any
one or more of the following characteristics:
   A.   Lacks an engine, wheel, tire, properly installed battery or other
structural parts which renders the vehicle inoperable for use as designed by
the manufacturer; provided, that if there is more than one vehicle on the real
property, there shall be the necessary number of engines, wheels, tires,
batteries and other structural parts for each respective vehicle;
   B.   Has a broken or missing fender, door, bumper, hood, exterior door
handle, running board, steering wheel, trunk top, trunk handle, tailpipe,
muffler, driver's seat, fuel tank, driveshaft, differential, generator,
alternator or other structural piece;
   C.   Has become or the potential to become the breeding ground or habitat of
rats, mice, snakes, mosquitoes or other vermin, rodents or insects, or is
otherwise used for the storage, harbor, caging or dwelling for an animal of any
kind;
   D.   Has heavy growth of weeds or other noxious vegetation over eight inches
(8") in height under or immediately next to it;
   E.   Has become a point of collection for stagnant water;
   F.   Has junk, garbage, refuse, gasoline or fuel other than in its fuel
tank, paper, cardboard, wood or other combustible materials, solid waste or
other hazardous material present in it or which is primarily used for storage
of any materials;
   G.   Has become a source of danger for children through entrapment in areas
of confinement that cannot be opened from inside, through a danger of the
vehicle falling or turning over, or through possible injury from exposed
surfaces of metal, glass or other rigid materials;
   H.   Has become a potential source of contamination of the soil from
petroleum products or other toxic liquids being discharged or leaking from the
vehicle;
   I.   Has become illegal to operate on the public streets because it is
missing one or more parts required by law;
   J.   Is an abandoned vehicle; or
   K.   Because of its defective, deteriorated or obsolete condition in any
other way constitutes a nuisance or a threat to the public's health or safety.
MACHINERY: Synonymous with and means the same as "machine" as defined by the
current edition of "Webster's New Collegiate Dictionary".
PARTS: Any mechanical, structural, body or decorative part of any vehicle,
machinery or trailer.
RESPONSIBLE PARTIES: Means:
   A.   If ascertainable, the last known registered owner of the junk vehicle
as indicated in the official records of the state of Montana department of
motor vehicles or a sister state division of transportation or motor vehicles.
TRAILER: Any vehicle without motive power designed for carrying persons or
property and for being drawn by a motor vehicle.
VEHICLE: Any device by which any person or property may be propelled, moved, or
drawn upon a street, except a device which is designed to be exclusively moved
by human power or used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. The term
vehicle shall include, but is not limited to, an automobile, truck, van, sports
utility vehicle, recreational vehicle camper, motorcycle, trailer, watercraft,
boat, canoe, jet skis, snowmobile, ATVs or aircraft. (Ord. 2003-05, 7-14-2003,
eff. 8-14-2003; amd. Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015)
5-7-3: EXEMPTIONS:
This chapter shall not apply to the following:
   A.   When such storage or parking is necessary to the operation of a
lawfully conducted business or commercial enterprise on land which such
business or enterprise is authorized by the city's zoning regulations;
   B.   A vehicle which was recently involved in a collision, duly documented
by a timely report filed with the appropriate law enforcement agency or the
state department of transportation, or its equivalent in a sister state, shall
not be deemed a junk vehicle unless the owner/operator of said vehicle fails to
repair the same within a reasonable period of time after said collision.
   C.   Nothing in this chapter shall authorize the maintenance of a public or
private nuisance as defined under provisions of law. Refer to criminal
nuisances in this code.
   D.   Nothing in this chapter and none of these exemptions alter any zoning
regulations for the land on which the vehicle is located. See title 12, "Zoning
Regulations", of this code. (Ord. 2003-05, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-14-2003)
5-7-4: JUNK VEHICLE DEEMED NUISANCE:
The keeping, maintaining or allowing a junk vehicle to be on public property or
illegally parked on private property, except as provided by section
5-7-3 of this chapter, shall constitute a nuisance. The owner of a junk vehicle
shall be responsible for the maintaining or keeping of a nuisance. (Ord. 2003-
05, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-14-2003)
5-7-5: ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT:
Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, the provisions of this chapter
shall be administered and enforced by the city's enforcement agency and/or
their respective designees, or city council designee, hereinafter collectively
referred to as the "enforcement officer". The enforcement officer and any
person designated to abate the nuisance pursuant to this code or court order,
are hereby authorized access to any property upon which a junk vehicle is
located for the purpose of carrying out any and all actions necessary to
enforce this chapter. (Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015)
5-7-6: ADMINISTRATION COSTS:
The city council shall determine and fix the administrative fee annually, an
amount to be assessed as administrative costs under this chapter. Said
administrative fee shall be in addition to the actual costs incurred regarding
towing, storage and disposal of the vehicle. The administrative fee shall be
set by resolution. (Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015)
5-7-7: NOTICES:
   A.   A ten (10) day notice (exclusive of weekends or federally mandated
holidays) of intention to abate and remove the vehicle or parts thereof as a
public nuisance shall be given to the owner of the vehicle, if known. The
notices of intention shall be in a form promulgated by the enforcement officer
and shall provide the following information at a minimum:
      1.   A description of the vehicle or parts which constitute(s) a nuisance
under the provisions of this code;
      2.   The nuisance must be abated within ten (10) days (exclusive of
weekends and federally mandated holidays). The junk vehicle must be either:
         a.   Brought into a condition that it no longer is defined as a "junk
vehicle";
         b.   Removed from the property and properly disposed of or removed
from the city; and
      3.   Failure to properly abate said nuisance as prescribed shall be
sufficient cause for the removal of the junk vehicle by the enforcement
authority or his/her duly designated agent as set forth by this Code.
   B.   The notice required by this section shall be served in any one of the
following manners:
      1.   Posting notice on or near the junk vehicle(s) in question and by
certified mail, return receipt requested, to the last registered owner of said
vehicle, if ascertainable, at the address listed in the State's records
concerning ownership of the vehicle (for the purposes of this provision service
shall be deemed to have been perfected the day after the notice is mailed); or
      2.   If the last registered owner's name is not ascertainable by posting
notice on or near the junk vehicle(s) in question (for the purposes of this
provision, service shall be deemed to have been perfected the day the notice is
posted on or near the junk vehicle). (Ord. 2003-05, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-14-2003)
5-7-8: ABATEMENT AND REMOVAL:
   A.   The responsible party, after service of notice is perfected, shall
abate the nuisance within ten (10) days (exclusive of weekends and Federally
mandated holidays) of service being perfected. Abatement shall consist of:
      1.   Providing for the current registration of each and every vehicle
including affixing the registration plate or current sticker to the vehicle;
      2.   Repairing any and all conditions which cause such vehicle(s) to be a
nuisance under the provisions of this Code; and
      3.   Having all of the required equipment and parts for each vehicle
which was described in the notice; or removing the junk vehicle or causing the
junk vehicle to be removed to the Rosebud County vehicle salvage yard or to a
licensed dismantler, salvage yard, licensed vehicle dealer, a junk dealer, an
auto body shop or to any other location provided the same complies with all
applicable provisions of this Code.
   B.   If the responsible parties fail to abate the nuisance as prescribed, or
after such abatement has been affirmed by the court on appeal, the City,
through the Enforcement Officer, may abate such nuisance by causing the junk
vehicle(s) to be removed, impounded and sold or disposed of as provided for
abandoned vehicles under the laws of the State of Montana. All costs of such
abatement and the administrative fee provided by this chapter shall be charged
to the responsible parties, jointly and severally. (Ord. 2003-05, 7-14-2003,
eff. 8-14-2003)
5-7-9: ILLEGAL OFF STREET PARKING:
   A.   No person shall park a vehicle onto or upon privately owned real
property or area developed as an off street parking facility without the
consent of the owner, lessee or person in charge of said property or facility.
   B.   No person shall park a vehicle onto or upon publicly owned real
property or area developed as an off street parking facility, if said property
is not properly designated and signed for parking of private vehicles; contrary
to any signs set forth upon said property or facility; or contrary to the laws
of the State of Montana, Rosebud County or the City of Forsyth, Montana,
without proper consent of said State, County or City.
   C.   Any vehicle parked in violation of this section shall be deemed an
abandoned vehicle. (Ord. 2003-05, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-14-2003)
5-7-10: CONTINUING NOTICE:
A notice issued as provided in section
5-7-7 of this chapter shall be deemed a continuing notice regarding the vehicle
(s) described in the notice for a period of one year from the date of service
and is valid for all locations within the City of Forsyth, Montana. No further
notice by an Enforcement Officer or ten (10) day period to abate is necessary
to abate a nuisance created by said vehicle(s) within the one year period.
(Ord. 2003-05, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-14-2003)
5-7-11: PENALTY:
   A.   Failure of the person or persons responsible for the accumulation and
storage of abandoned, wrecked, junked or dismantled or inoperative vehicles,
machinery, trailers, or parts thereof on public property or illegally parked on
private property which has not been abated as such in accordance with the
provisions of this chapter within the time specified in the notice, after the
same has been served as provided in this chapter, constitutes a violation of
this chapter. Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal
infractions as specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code.
   B.   In any action or proceeding brought for the violation of this chapter,
as defined in this chapter, the reasonable cost and expense to City in
connection with the mailing or serving of notice and the inspection of the
private property in question, shall be awarded to City as part of the court's
judgment. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
5-7-12: NONEXCLUSIVE OF THIS CHAPTER:
This chapter is not the exclusive regulation of abandoned, wrecked, dismantled
or inoperative vehicles within the City of Forsyth, Montana. It shall
supplement and be in addition to the other regulatory codes, statutes, and
ordinances heretofore or hereafter enacted by the City, the State, or any other
legal entity or agency having jurisdiction. (Ord. 2003-05, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-
14-2003)
CHAPTER 8
UNSAFE SIGNS
SECTION:
5-8-1: Definitions
5-8-2: Purpose
5-8-3: Prohibition
5-8-4: Maintenance
5-8-5: Removal
5-8-6: Abandoned Signs
5-8-7: Penalty
5-8-1: DEFINITIONS:
ABANDONED SIGN: A sign remaining in place for at least thirty (30) days after
it no longer advertises or identifies an ongoing business, product, or service
available on the premises where the sign is located.
SIGN: Any identification, description, illustration or device, illuminated or
nonilluminated, which is visible from any public place or is located on private
property and exposed to the public and which directs attention to a produce,
service, place, activity, person, institution, business or solicitation,
including any permanently installed or situated merchandise, or any emblem,
painting, banner, pennant, placard or temporary sign designed to advertise,
identify or convey information, with the exception of window display and
national flags. "Signs" shall also include all sign structures. (Ord. 2003-09,
10-27-2003, eff. 11-27-2003)
5-8-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to establish standards for the removal of any
abandoned, unsafe, or dangerous business signs. (Ord. 2003-09, 10-27-2003, eff.
11-27-2003)
5-8-3: PROHIBITION:
Prohibition shall be a violation of this chapter to maintain an unsafe,
dangerous, or abandoned sign. (Ord. 2003-09, 10-27-2003, eff. 11-27-2003)
5-8-4: MAINTENANCE:
All signs shall be maintained in an operable and safe condition. Failure to
comply with the maintenance provision of this chapter shall constitute a
violation. (Ord. 2003-09, 10-27-2003, eff. 11-27-2003)
5-8-5: REMOVAL:
   The Code Enforcement Officer or building inspector shall require the removal
of any sign found to be unsafe or unmaintained except for emergencies. Before
bringing such action to require the removal of an unmaintained sign, the Code
Enforcement Officer or building inspector shall provide written notice to the
owner of the sign or the owner of the premises on which the sign is located.
The notice shall state the reason for the removal, specifying the deficiency
and violations and such notice shall specify what repairs, if any, to make the
sign safe. Notice shall be made to the owner of record either by personal
service or by certified mail.
   If the owner or lessee fails to remove the sign within the allowed time
after written notice, the Code Enforcement Officer or building inspector is
authorized to remove the sign at the owner’s expense.
   If the Code Enforcement Officer or building inspector finds that any sign or
sign support is in violation of this section, and by reason of its condition it
presents an immediate danger to the public, he shall order that the sign be
immediately removed. If the person who is responsible cannot be found, the Code
Enforcement Officer or building inspector should remove the sign within ten
(10) days of the notification.
(Ord. 2003-09, 10-27-2003, eff. 11-27-2003; amd. Ord. 2024-06, 12-16-2024)
5-8-6: ABANDONED SIGNS:
Any person who owns or leases a building, which has a sign shall remove the
sign within thirty (30) days after it becomes abandoned as defined in this
chapter. If the owner or lessee cannot be located, the city shall remove such
sign. The cost of removal shall be borne by the owner of the sign.
A building, structure, or premises shall be determined to be vacated based upon
the following criteria:
   A.   Vacancy.
   B.   Cessation of utility services.
   C.   Termination of the business license.
Sign structures that have been left vacant, devoid of any messages, display a
message pertaining to a time, event, or purpose that no longer applies, or are
unoccupied, any of which for a thirty (30) day period shall be deemed abandoned
and must be removed. (Ord. 2003-09, 10-27-2003, eff. 11-27-2003)
5-8-7: PENALTY:
Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as specified
in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 9
COMMUNITY DECAY
SECTION:
5-9-1: Definitions
5-9-2: Decay Prohibited
5-9-3: Shielding
5-9-4: Jurisdiction
5-9-5: Compatibility
5-9-6: Penalty
5-9-1: DEFINITIONS:
   A.   In this chapter the following terms have the meaning indicated below:
    ACCUMULATE: To gather, collect, heap or pile up.
   COMMUNITY DECAY: A public nuisance created by allowing rubble, debris, junk,
junk vehicle(s), dangerous structure(s), or refuse to accumulate on or adjacent
to a public right of way so that it:
      1.   Endangers safety or health, is offensive to the senses, or obstructs
the free use of property so as to interfere with the comfortable enjoyment of
life or property.
      2.   Is a condition which renders dangerous for passage on any public
right of way.
Community decay does not include persons servicing, manufacturing, or
processing materials, goods, or products on lots in public view, so long as the
materials used in the normal operation of the business are neatly stacked,
piled or shredded, and such businesses are conducted within a properly zoned
area. Community decay does not include normal residential maintenance or
landscaping.
   PERSON: An individual, firm, partnership, company, association, corporation,
city, town, local governmental entity, or any other governmental or private
