entity, whether organized for profit or not.
   PUBLIC NUISANCE: A nuisance which affects, at the same time, an entire
community or neighborhood or any considerable number of persons, although the
extent of the annoyance or damage inflicted upon individuals may be unequal.
   SHIELDING: Refers to fencing or other manmade barriers to conceal community
decay from public view. It also refers to natural barriers. Any shielding
barrier must conform to all local zoning, planning, building, and protective
covenant provisions. Any shielding is to be of sufficient height so that none
of the violations on the premises is visible to public view. This is not
intended to require that permanent buildings, other structures, or utility
poles be included in this and be shielded. (Ord. 2003-10, 11-10-2003, eff. 12-
10-2003)
5-9-2: DECAY PROHIBITED:
   A.   It shall be a violation of this chapter to own or maintain any public
nuisance or community decay.
      1.   No person shall dump, pile, or stack bricks, concrete, block, waste
wood, and similar material in public view unless said material is stacked in
neat piles and all waste material from the cleaning of such items, such as
mortar, wood splinters, broken and unusable bricks, is removed to a licensed
solid waste disposal facility or to some other location which has been approved
by the city of Forsyth within thirty (30) days.
      2.   No person shall store or accumulate cardboard boxes, broken packing
boxes, paper, broken shipping pallets, tires, rubble, debris, junk refuse, dead
animals or animal parts, except animal parts used for ornamental purposes, or
other similar items in public view.
      3.   No person shall pile, dump, or deposit any dirt, demolition wastes
including wood, bricks, concrete, and other similar materials in public view,
unless such material is to be utilized for fill material to fill a land
depression. If such material is used as fill material, it may contain only
dirt, bricks, or concrete and all such material must be completely covered with
clean fill material once every thirty (30) days and the fill area adequately
fenced to restrict access to the area.
      4.   No person shall store or accumulate iron, metal, machine parts,
household appliances, barrels, and/or other salvaged metal items in public
view.
      5.   No person shall accumulate or store any other rubble, debris, junk,
or refuse that, upon investigation is deemed to be a "public nuisance" as
defined in this chapter.
      6.   No person shall accumulate, leave or permit to remain outside of any
dwelling, building or other structure or within any unoccupied or abandoned
building, structure or dwelling under his control, in a place accessible to
children any storage items, refrigerators, freezers or containers that
constitute an attractive hazard as defined herein without first removing said
door or lid, snaplock or other locking device. (Ord. 2003-10, 11-10-2003, eff.
12-10-2003)
      7.   No person shall permit or suffer to be in or accumulate in or upon
any yard, lot, place or premises or upon any street or sidewalk adjacent to or
abutting upon any lot, block, place or premises or in any building or shed
owned or occupied by him for which he may be an agent within the limit of the
city, any stagnant water or impure water, refuse, vegetable decay or decaying
substance, garbage or filth of any kind, nor suffer such yard, lot, place,
building or premises to be or to remain in such condition as to cause or create
a nuisance or offensive smell or to pollute or render unhealthful the
atmosphere or the premises or thereby to be, become, cause or create a public
nuisance. It shall be the responsibility of the public works director and/or a
city council designee to enforce the provisions of this title. (Ord. 2015-06,
9-28-2015)
      8.   No person shall allow storage of junk or abandoned vehicles as
defined in the junk vehicle ordinance.
   B.   Regardless of any provision of this chapter to the contrary if a person
engages in any of the activities listed in this section as an ongoing
continuous salvage business, the business shall be located in an area properly
zoned for such a salvage business and shall be shielded from public view as
required by this chapter. (Ord. 2003-10, 11-10-2003, eff. 12-10-2003)
5-9-3: SHIELDING:
   A.   The maintenance of materials that would be considered a public nuisance
under this chapter shall be lawful if such materials are shielded from public
view and if such shielding otherwise serves to abate the nuisance that is being
complained about. (Ord. 2003-10, 11-10-2003, eff. 12-10-2003)
      1.   Any shielding must conform to all local zoning, planning, building
code and protective covenant provisions applicable to the property and shall be
sufficient height that none of the nuisance materials on the premises are
visible to public view. There may be situations where partial shielding is
allowed. This determination will be made by the enforcement officer. (Ord.
2015-06, 9-28-2015)
      2.   No more than one shielding material shall be used on any one side of
a shielding fence unless approved by the city. (Ord. 2003-10, 11-10-2003, eff.
12-10-2003)
5-9-4: JURISDICTION:
   A.   This chapter applies to the incorporated limits of the city of Forsyth.
(Ord. 2003-10, 11-10-2003, eff. 12-10-2003)
5-9-5: COMPATIBILITY:
Nothing in this chapter or Montana Code Annotated section 7-5-2110 may be
construed to abrogate or affect the provisions of any lawful ordinance,
regulation or resolution that is more restrictive than the provisions of this
chapter or Montana Code Annotated section 7-5-2110. (Ord. 2003-10, 11-10-2003,
eff. 12-10-2003)
5-9-6: PENALTY:
Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as specified
in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code.
(Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 10
SHIPPING CONTAINERS/CONEX BOXES
SECTION:
5-10-1: Nuisance Declared
5-10-2: Enforcement
5-10-3: Penalty
5-10-4: Shipping Containers/Conex Boxes Allowed
5-10-5: Conditional Use Permit Required
5-10-6: Parameters For The Use Of Shipping Containers/Conex Boxes
5-10-7: Removal Of Storage Containers/Conex Boxes
5-10-8: Failure To Remove Storage Container/Conex Boxes
5-10-1: NUISANCE DECLARED:
The use of shipping containers as storage or buildings on private property has
increased in the city. Shipping containers and similar structures pose a risk
to individuals and the public because they are not securely anchored, are not
served with adequate utilities, do not have fire suppression systems, do not
contain adequate ventilation and generally have heavy doors or other opening
mechanisms that may be difficult to operate. (Ord. 2022-04, 7-25-2022)
5-10-2: ENFORCEMENT:
The provisions of this article shall be enforced as provided in Montana Code
Annotated and City of Forsyth code. (Ord. 2022-04, 7-25-2022)
5-10-3: PENALTY:
Violations of this chapter are designed as Municipal infractions as specified
in
title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2022-04, 7-25-2022)
5-10-4: SHIPPING CONTAINERS/CONEX BOXES ALLOWED:
One (1) bin shall be allowed on properties that are zoned highway commercial
without a conditional use permit request. More than one container in high
commercial zoned areas will require a conditional use permit.
(Ord. 2022-04, 7-25-2022; amd. Ord. 2022-07, 1-16-2023)
5-10-5: CONDITIONAL USE PERMIT REQUIRED:
All containers in any zoning area other than highway commercial will require a
conditional use permit.
(Ord. 2022-04, 7-25-2022; amd. Ord. 2022-07, 1-16-2023)
5-10-6: PARAMETERS FOR THE USE OF SHIPPING CONTAINERS/CONEX BOXES:
   A.   All approved containers must be located in the rear or side of the lot
and any existing home or structure;
   B.   All building and zoning codes apply which include but are not limited
to: all front/back/side set -backs; permits, 50/50 rule, IBC's preventing
buildings and structures over utilities and other applicable cods and rules;
   C.   Containers must be kept painted in a color that matches or conforms to
other structures on the existing property;
   D.   Containers must only be used for storage and in no way will they be
used for habitation;
   E.   A concrete foundation or appropriate footings must be in place to
prevent the container from settling into the ground;
   F.   Previous usage verification must be provided to ensure that the
container was not used to house or transfer and hazardous or radioactive
materials. (Ord. 2022-04, 7-25-2022)
5-10-7: REMOVAL OF STORAGE CONTAINERS/CONEX BOXES:
   A.   Any property owner with a storage container(s)/conex boxes on property
within the City shall have sixty (60) days from the date of passage of this
section to remove such storage container/conex box or to obtain a conditional
use permit for the use of the storage container/conex box.
(Ord. 2022-04, 7-25-2022; amd. Ord. 2022-07, 1-16-2023)
5-10-8: FAILURE TO REMOVE STORAGE CONTAINER/CONEX BOXES:
Failure to remove any unpermitted storage container/conex box before the
expiration of the 60-day period shall be deemed a violation of Title 5, Chapter
10 and any citizen will be subject to enforcement and penalty described
therein. (Ord. 2022-04, 7-25-2022)
CHAPTER 11
ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
5-11-1: Administration And Enforcement
5-11-2: Administration Costs
5-11-3: Notices
5-11-4: Abatement And Removal
5-11-5: Penalty
5-11-1: ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT:
Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, the provisions of this title
shall be administered and enforced by city's enforcement agency and/or their
respective designees, or city council designee hereinafter collectively
referred to as the "enforcement officer". The enforcement officer and any
person designated to abate the nuisance pursuant to this code or court order,
are hereby authorized access to any property for the purpose of carrying out
any and all actions necessary to enforce this title. (Ord. 2015-08, 12-21-2015)
5-11-2: ADMINISTRATION COSTS:
The city council shall determine and fix the administrative fee, an amount to
be assessed as administrative costs under this chapter. Said administrative fee
shall be in addition to the actual costs incurred in the enforcement of this
title. The administrative fee shall be set by resolution. (Ord. 2015-08, 12-21-
2015)
5-11-3: NOTICES:
   A.   A ten (10) day notice (exclusive of weekends or federally mandated
holidays) of intention to abate the described nuisance shall be given to the
alleged offender, if known. The notices of intention shall be in a form
promulgated by the enforcement officer and shall provide the following
information at a minimum:
      1.   A description of the items, issues or parts which constitute(s) a
nuisance under the provisions of this code;
      2.   The nuisance must be abated within ten (10) days (exclusive of
weekends and federally mandated holidays).
         a.   Brought into a condition that it no longer is defined as a
nuisance.
         b.   Removed from the property and properly disposed of or removed
from the city.
      3.   Failure to properly abate said nuisance as prescribed shall be
sufficient cause for the removal of the nuisance by the enforcement authority
or his/her duly designated agent as set forth by this code.
   B.   The notice required by this section shall be served in any one of the
following manners:
      1.   Posting notice on or near the nuisance in question and by certified
mail, return receipt requested, to the last known owner of the nuisance or
affected property, if ascertainable, at the address listed in available records
(for the purposes of this provision, service shall be deemed to have been
perfected the day after the notice is mailed); or
      2.   If the last owner's name is not ascertainable, by posting notice on
or near the nuisance(s) in question (for the purposes of this provision,
service shall be deemed to have been perfected the day the notice is posted).
(Ord. 2015-08, 12-21-2015)
5-11-4: ABATEMENT AND REMOVAL:
   A.   The responsible party, after service of notice is perfected, shall
abate the nuisance within ten (10) days (exclusive of weekends and federally
mandated holidays) of service being perfected.
   B.   If the responsible parties fail to abate the nuisance as prescribed, or
after such nonabatement has been affirmed by the court on appeal, the city,
through the enforcement officer, may abate such nuisance by causing the
nuisance(s) to be removed, impounded and sold or disposed of. All costs of such
abatement and the administrative fee provided by this chapter shall be charged
to the responsible parties, jointly and severally. (Ord. 2015-08, 12-21-2015)
5-11-5: PENALTY:
Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as specified
in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
TITLE 6
FIRE REGULATIONS 1
CHAPTER 1
FIRE PREVENTION CODE
SECTION:
6-1-1: Adoption Of Fire Prevention Code
6-1-2: Stove Inspections; Fee
 
Notes
1 1. MCA title 7, chapter 33.
6-1-1: ADOPTION OF FIRE PREVENTION CODE:
For the purpose of regulating and governing conditions hazardous to life and
property from fire, the fire prevention code, current edition, as recommended
by the National Board Of Fire Underwriters, is hereby adopted. Said fire
prevention code, one copy of which shall be on file at all times in the office
of the city clerk-treasurer, shall be made a part of this code as if set out at
length herein. (Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015)
6-1-2: STOVE INSPECTIONS; FEE:
In the event any request is made by the owner or insurance carrier of an
existing wood or coal burning stove in the city, the building inspector is
henceforth authorized to perform inspections of those stoves and a fee of
twenty dollars ($20.00) shall be assessed, fifteen dollars ($15.00) for the
building inspector and five dollars ($5.00) for the city. These inspections are
to be on a voluntary basis only, are not to be performed unless requested by
the owner or insurance carrier for a home that has a wood or coal burning stove
and are not designed to limit or eliminate inspections of a similar type
performed by any other person or insurance carrier for a home that has a coal
or wood burning stove. (Res., 12-28-1987)
CHAPTER 2
FIREWORKS
SECTION:
6-2-1: Defined
6-2-2: Dates And Locations Fireworks Prohibited
6-2-3: Exceptions
6-2-4: Penalty
6-2-1: DEFINED:
The city adopts by reference the state of Montana definition of "fireworks" as
set forth in Montana Code Annotated section 50-37-101.
(MCA § 50-37-101 (2019)) (Ord. 2021-02, 9-27-2021; amd. Ord. 2023-01, 1-8-2024)
6-2-2: DATES AND LOCATIONS FIREWORKS PROHIBITED:
In addition to authority under Montana law:
   A.   Sale Of Fireworks: It shall be unlawful for any person to sell any
fireworks except on the following dates:
      June 24 through July 5 each year; and
      December 29 through December 31 each year.
   B.   Location Restrictions On Discharge Of Fireworks: It shall be unlawful
for any person to discharge or cause to be discharged any fireworks in the
following locations at all times:
      Main Street
      Front Street
   C.   Time Restrictions On Discharge Of Fireworks: It shall be unlawful for
any person to discharge or cause to be discharged any fireworks within the
exterior boundaries of the City of Forsyth except on the following dates and
times:
      1.   July 1 through July 4:
      The times and dates that it is permissible to detonate, combust or
display legally authorized fireworks is from July 1 through July 4 from eleven
(11:00) A.M. to eleven (11:00) P.M., except that fireworks will be allowed to
be detonated until twelve (12:00) midnight on July 4.
      2.   In addition, fireworks will be allowed to be detonated on New Year’s
Eve, from four o’clock (4:00) P.M. December 31 through twelve thirty o’clock
(12:30) A.M. January 1.
   D.   Permit Required:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any vendor to sell fireworks within the
exterior boundaries of the City of Forsyth without first obtaining a business
license from the City Clerk. Vendors who obtain a business license to sell
fireworks within the City of Forsyth may only sell fireworks between June 24
and July 5, and December 29 and December 31 each year as provided for under
Montana Code Annotated section 50-37-106.
      2.   Vendors who obtain a permit to sell fireworks within the City of
Forsyth must strictly comply with all requirements of State law.
(Ord. 2011-02, 10-24-2011; Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015; Ord. 2021-02, 9-27-2021;
Ord. 2023-01, 1-8-2024; Ord. 2024-01, 12-16-2024)
6-2-3: EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   Signaling Devices: Nothing in this chapter shall be held to apply to
the possession or use of signaling devices for current daily consumption by
railroads, trucks and others requiring them.
   B.   Displays; Permit Required: The Chief of the Fire Department may, upon
due application, issue a permit to a properly qualified person for giving a
pyrotechnic display in the public parks or other open places. The permit will
be acquired from City Hall, and the Fire Chief must sign off on the permit.
(Ord. 2015-06, 9-28-2015; Ord. 2021-02, 9-27-2021; Ord. 2023-01, 1-8-2024)
6-2-4: PENALTY:
Violations of the time and location restrictions in this chapter are designated
as Municipal infractions as specified in
title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. All other violations are considered
misdemeanors and punishable as set forth in this code.
(Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019; Ord. 2021-02, 9-27-2021; Ord. 2023-
01, 1-8-2024)
CHAPTER 3
FIRE SAFETY REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-3-1: Public Buildings
6-3-2: Open Burning; Permission Required; Violation
6-3-3: Open Burning; Bonfire Restrictions
6-3-4: Special Burn Permit
6-3-5: Recreational Fire Pit
6-3-6: Clean Burning Fuels
6-3-7: Functional Water Source
6-3-8: Open Burning Prohibited
6-3-9: Constantly Attended
6-3-10: Liability For Damages
6-3-11: Unlawful Open Burning
6-3-12: Enforcement
6-3-13: Penalty
6-3-1: PUBLIC BUILDINGS:
Pursuant to sections 7-5-108, 7-5-109, 7-5-4202 and 7-33-4208, Montana Code
Annotated, the City hereby adopts and includes within this Code, by this
reference, title 50, chapter 61, Montana Code Annotated, entitled Fire Safety
in Public Buildings, the same being sections 50-61-101 through 50-61-121,
Montana Code Annotated, inclusive. (Res. 1990-R11, 11-12-1990)
6-3-2: OPEN BURNING; PERMISSION REQUIRED; VIOLATION:
It shall be unlawful for any person to burn any debris or material outside a
dwelling house without first obtaining permission from the County Sheriff's
Office. Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as
specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff.
1-1-2019)
6-3-3: OPEN BURNING; BONFIRE RESTRICTIONS:
Bonfires restrictions apply within the city limits of Forsyth:
   A.   Fires which exceed the size of a recreational fire are bonfires and are
not permitted within the city limits of Forsyth, unless a special burn permit
is obtained and is approved by the Forsyth city council. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-
2022)
6-3-4: SPECIAL BURN PERMIT:
An Application for a special burn permit can be obtained at City Hall
Permission and verification from the Forsyth Volunteer Fire-Department is
required. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-2022)
6-3-5: RECREATIONAL FIRE PIT:
A recreational fire pit may be conducted in a homemade/unlisted (non-
commercially available/produced incinerator, commercially available fire pit,
outdoor fireplace, fire pit, portable outdoor fireplace, barbeque grill,
barbeque pit when it is constructed of and surrounded by wholly noncombustible
materials. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-2022)
6-3-6: CLEAN BURNING FUELS:
Only clean burning fuels such as unpainted wood, paper, paper goods, cardboard,
pellets, propane or charcoal may be used. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-2022)
6-3-7: FUNCTIONAL WATER SOURCE:
Must have a functional water source and garden hose, appropriately sized
extinguisher or other comparable means of fire extinguishment immediately
available at all times. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-2022)
6-3-8: OPEN BURNING PROHIBITED:
May be prohibited based on hazardous conditions such as severe weather or
drought. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-2022)
6-3-9: CONSTANTLY ATTENDED:
Must be constantly attended until completely extinguished. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-
2022)
6-3-10: LIABILITY FOR DAMAGES:
A person who sets or leaves a fire that spreads and damages or destroys
property of any kind not belonging to the person (or threatens to do the same)
may be held liable for all damages caused by the fie and all costs and expenses
incurred, but not limited to, expenses incurred in fire suppression and
investigation. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-2022)
6-3-11: UNLAWFUL OPEN BURNING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to openly burn any debris or material
outside of the allowances described in
6-3-2 within the city limits of the City of Forsyth. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-2022)
6-3-12: ENFORCEMENT:
The provisions of this article shall be enforced as provided in Montana Code
Annotated and City of Forsyth code. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-2022)
6-3-13: PENALTY:
Violations of this chapter are designed as Municipal infractions as specified
in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2022-03, 8-8-2022)
TITLE 7
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
7-1-1: State Criminal Code Adopted
7-1-2: Barbed Wire And Electric Fences
7-1-3: Loudspeakers Or Sound Trucks (Rep. by Ord. 2024-07, 12-16-2024)
