7-1-1: STATE CRIMINAL CODE ADOPTED:
The City adopts the Montana Criminal Code of 1973, Montana Code Annotated
section 45-1-101, et seq., except insofar as the application thereof is clearly
impractical or inappropriate. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
7-1-2: BARBED WIRE AND ELECTRIC FENCES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to erect or maintain any electric fence. It
is further unlawful for any person to erect any fence constructed in whole or
in part of barbed wire or to use barbed wire as a guard to any parking lot or
parcel of land; provided, however, the City Council may, in specific instances
upon request, grant a written license to erect certain barbed wire fences or
structures within the City limits for protective purposes, if in the judgment
of the City Council, the erection of said barbed wire fence is in the interest
of public safety or is an adjunct to law enforcement; further provided,
however, in the event the City Council elects to approve the erection of a
barbed wire fence under the exceptions herein provided, the licensee will be
obligated to provide to the City an indemnifying agreement holding the City
harmless for any bodily injury or property damage resulting from the erection
and maintenance of said fence, or in lieu thereof, a bond or such other
security as the City Council may require. Violations of this section are
designated as Municipal infractions as specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this
Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
7-1-3: LOUDSPEAKERS OR SOUND TRUCKS:
(Rep. by Ord. 2024-07, 12-16-2024)
7-1-4: LUG WHEELS:
It shall be unlawful for tractors or other vehicles equipped with wheels
injurious to pavement to be permitted upon the public thoroughfares. Vehicles
must have lug nut covers. Violations of this section are designated as
Municipal infractions as specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord.
2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
7-1-5: PLAYING BALL ON STREETS:
(Rep. by Ord. 2024-07, 12-16-2024)
7-1-6: DRINKING IN PUBLIC PLACES; DISPLAY 1 :
   A.   Definitions: The following words and phrases used in this section shall
be defined as follows:
    BEER: Shall mean and be defined as that term is defined in the Alcoholic
Beverage Code by section 16-1-106, Montana Code Annotated, as amended.
   LIQUOR OR LIQUORS: Shall mean and be defined as those terms are defined by
section 16-1-106, Montana Code Annotated, as amended, of the Alcoholic Beverage
Code.
   PUBLIC DISPLAY OR EXHIBITIONISM OF BEER OR LIQUOR: The carrying and
exhibiting of opened cans or bottles of beer or the carrying and exhibiting of
glasses or containers containing beer or liquor, even though empty, from retail
liquor or beer establishments to, in, on or upon the public places in the City,
but does not include carrying or transporting such beer or liquor from retail
liquor or beer establishments in sacks, cases, boxes or cartons when no display
or exhibition is made.
   PUBLIC DRINKING: The drinking or consuming of beer or liquor in, on or upon
the public places in the City.
   PUBLIC PLACES: The streets, avenues, alleys and places in the City, but does
not include the premises licensed for the sale of liquor or beer at retail by
the Montana Liquor Control Board, nor does it include private residences and
other private places not within the public view. (Ord. 186, 10-14-1963)
   B.   Public Drinking And Display Prohibited; Violation: "Public drinking"
and "public display or exhibitionism of beer or liquor", as defined in
subsection A of this section, is hereby prohibited and it shall be unlawful for
any person to engage in "public drinking", as herein defined, within the City
limits, and it shall be unlawful for any person to engage in "public display or
exhibitionism of beer or liquor", as herein defined, within the City limits.
Violations of this section shall be considered a misdemeanor and punishable as
set forth in this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
 
Notes
1 1. See section 8-5-1 of this Code for variance provisions.
7-1-7: EXOTIC DANCERS; NUDE AND SEMINUDE EXHIBITIONS:
   A.   Unlawful; Described: The dances or exhibitions referred to in this
section shall not be deemed unlawful unless:
      1.   Any female participant intentionally appears with breast or breasts
uncovered. The breast shall be considered under the prohibitions of this
section when any portion of the nipple or areola is not covered by a fully
opaque material or is so thinly covered as to appear uncovered.
      2.   Any person, male or female, appears unclothed, costumed or clothed
in such a manner that the lower part of his or her torso, consisting of the
private parts or genitalia, or anal cleft or cleavage of the buttocks, is not
covered by a fully opaque material or is so thinly covered as to appear
uncovered. (Ord., eff. 2-15-1985)
   B.   Penalty: Any person procuring or employing any person to participate in
such prohibited dances or exhibitions is guilty of a misdemeanor and upon
conviction thereof, subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. Additionally, any person who participates, for hire or
voluntarily, in any such dance or exhibition, contrary to the mandate of this
section, is guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof, subject to
penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord., eff. 2-15-1985; amd. 1999 Code)
7-1-8: SANITATION VIOLATION:
Any person who shall urinate or defecate in any public place, other than a
public restroom or toilet, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction
thereof, subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. Such offense is declared to be a violation of the public
health and sanitation standards of the City. (Ord., eff. 6-23-1980; amd. 1999
Code)
7-1-9: DIKE PRESERVATION:
   A.   Deterioration Unlawful: It shall be unlawful for any person to perform
any activity which may cause a deterioration of the Yellowstone River dike or
any vegetation on said dike. Violations of this section shall be considered a
misdemeanor and punishable as set forth in this Code.
   B.   Protected Area: The length of the dike to be so protected shall include
that part of the Yellowstone River dike running from the West Rosebud Fishing
Access to the waste water treatment plant.
(Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019; amd. Ord. 2024-07, 12-16-2024)
7-1-10: LITTERING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to throw, deposit, dump or leave any
garbage, debris, refuge, dead animal, including bottles, cans, glass, nails,
wire, paper or any other substance in or upon any street, alley, private
property of another or upon any public property under the control of any
governmental or political subdivision within the City. Violations of this
section shall be considered a misdemeanor and punishable as set forth in this
Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
7-1-11: QUIET HOURS ESTABLISHED:
   A.   The hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. to six o'clock (6:00) A.M. are
hereby established as quiet hours in the City of Forsyth, and it is unlawful to
create excessive noise, such as loud music (including from vehicles), from
either residences or vehicles, operation of machinery, including lawn mowers
and chain saws, and other activities which adversely affect the use and quiet
enjoyment by citizens by their residential houses during these hours. (Ord.
2002-10, 11-12-2002, eff. 12-12-2002)
   B.   Violations of this section are designated as Municipal infractions as
specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff.
1-1-2019)
7-1-12: ABANDONED VEHICLES:
   A.   Any vehicle that is removed through enforcement action of the City,
whether the removal is from either public or private property, creates a prima
facie presumption that the last registered owner of the vehicle is responsible
for the abandonment and is liable for all costs incurred in the removing,
storing, and disposing of the abandoned vehicle. The following costs and
proceedings are adopted:
      1.   Towing Fee: The actual amount charged by the contractor hired by the
City for removal of the vehicle. This amount shall not exceed what is
considered commercially reasonable.
      2.   Storage: The City of Forsyth is authorized to charge up to ten
dollars ($10.00) per day, up to a total of one hundred dollars ($100.00), for
storing such impounded vehicles.
      3.   Other Expenses: Any other actual expenses directly incurred by the
storage of the vehicle.
      4.   Payment: All charges will be paid to the City Treasurer, and proof
of payment shown before the vehicle is released.
      5.   Placement Of Vehicles: Abandoned vehicles will be stored on City
property.
      6.   Enforcement: The Rosebud County Sheriff is designated as the law
enforcement agency responsible for enforcement. (Ord. 2008-01, 1-28-2008, eff.
2-28-2008)
      7.   Violation: Violations of this section are designated as Municipal
infractions as specified in
title 1, chapter 4 of this Code.
(Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
7-1-13: UNLAWFUL PARKING:
   A.   Stopping, standing, or parking prohibited in specified places -
- exceptions -- definition.
      1.   a.   A person may not stop, stand, or park a vehicle, except when
necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with law or the
directions of a police officer, highway patrol officer, or official traffic
control device, in any of the following places:
            (1)   On a sidewalk;
            (2)   In front of a public or private driveway;
            (3)   Within an intersection;
            (4)   Within 15 feet of a fire hydrant;
            (5)   On a crosswalk;
            (6)   Within 20 feet of a crosswalk at an intersection;
            (7)   Within 30 feet upon the approach to any flashing beacon, stop
sign, or official traffic control device located at the side of a roadway;
            (8)   Between a safety zone and the adjacent curb or within 30 feet
of points on the curb immediately opposite the ends of a safety zone, unless
the local authorities indicate a different length by signs or markings;
            (9)   Within 50 feet of the nearest rail of a railroad crossing;
            (10)   Within 20 feet of the driveway entrance to any fire station
and on the side of a street opposite the entrance to any fire station within 75
feet of the entrance when properly signposted;
            (11)   Alongside or opposite any street excavation or obstruction
when stopping, standing, or parking would obstruct traffic;
            (12)   On the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the
edge or curb of a street;
            (13)   Upon any bridge or other elevated structure upon a highway
or within a highway tunnel;
            (14)   At any place where official traffic control devices prohibit
stopping.
         b.   A public bus stop may not be established in the areas described
in subsections (1)(a) through (1)(c) and (1)(e). Otherwise, this section does
not prohibit the establishment of public bus stops and the regulation of their
use by the authority having jurisdiction. A bus stop may only be established
pursuant to a traffic and engineering study.
         c.   A person may not move a vehicle not lawfully under the person’s
control into a prohibited area or an unlawful distance away from a curb.
         d.   As used in this section, “safety zone” means the area or space
that is officially set apart within a roadway for the exclusive use of
pedestrians and that is protected or is so marked or indicated by adequate
signs as to be plainly visible at all times while set apart as a safety zone.
   (MCA 61-8-354)
History: En. Sec. 98, Ch. 263, L. 1955; R.C.M. 1947, 32-21-101; amd. Sec. 1,
Ch. 417, L. 1981; amd. Sec. 6, Ch. 450, L. 1983; amd. Sec. 1, Ch. 217, L. 1989;
amd. Sec. 3, Ch. 512, L. 1991; amd. Secs. 33, 51(1), Ch. 352, L. 2003; amd.
Sec. 201, Ch. 542, L. 2005.
      2.   No person shall park any vehicle in a driveway that obstructs the
sidewalk and impedes the ability for pedestrians to walk on the sidewalk, or
wheelchair access on the sidewalk, due to the size of the vehicle or position
parked.
      3.   No person shall park on a boulevard owned by the city.
      4.   No person shall park any vehicle upon a street in such a manner or
under such conditions as to leave available less than ten (10) feet of the
width of the roadway for free movement of vehicular traffic at all times.
      5.   No person shall stop, stand or park any vehicle within an alley for
a period of time longer than 20 minutes for the reasonably expeditious loading
or unloading of such vehicle.
      6.   No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle within an alley in
such a manner or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten (10)
feet of the width of the roadway for the free movement of vehicular traffic.
      7.   No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle within an alley in
such a position as to block the driveway or entrance to any abutting property.
(Ord. 2024-07, 12-16-2024)
CHAPTER 2
CURFEW
SECTION:
7-2-1: Restrictions
7-2-2: Responsibility Of Parents
7-2-3: Violations; Penalty
7-2-1: RESTRICTIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any minor under the age of eighteen (18) years to
loiter, idle, wander, stroll, or drive, operate or ride in an automobile
randomly, purposelessly or aimlessly, in or upon the public street, highways,
roads, alleys, parks, playgrounds, other public grounds, or other public places
or other unsupervised places, between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and
five o'clock (5:00) A.M. of the following day, official City time, Sunday
through Thursday, from September 1 to June 1, and between the hours of ten
thirty o'clock (10:30) P.M. and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. of the following day,
official City time, Sunday through Thursday from June 1 to September 1, and
between twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. of the
following day, on Friday and Saturday nights throughout the year; provided
however, that the provisions of this section do not apply to a minor
accompanied by his parent, guardian or other adult person having the care and
custody of the minor or where the minor is upon an emergency errand or
legitimate business directed by his or her parent, guardian or other adult
person having the care and custody of the minor. (Ord. 178, 1958; amd. Ord.
178, 3-28-1966)
7-2-2: RESPONSIBILITY OF PARENTS:
It shall be unlawful for the parent, guardian or other adult person having the
care and custody of a minor under the age of eighteen (18) years to allow or
permit such minor to loiter, idle, wander, stroll or drive, operate or ride in
an automobile randomly, purposelessly or aimlessly in or upon the public
streets, highways, roads, alleys, parks, playgrounds, other public grounds,
other public places or other unsupervised places, during those hours when the
same is prohibited as defined in section
7-2-1 of this chapter; provided however, that the provisions of this section do
not apply when the minor is accompanied by his parent, guardian or other adult
person having the care and custody of the minor or where the minor is upon an
emergency errand or legitimate business directed by his or her parent, guardian
or other adult person having the care and custody of the minor. (Ord. 178,
1958; amd. Ord. 178, 3-28-1966)
7-2-3: VIOLATIONS; PENALTY:
   A.   Duty To Apprehend: It shall be the duty of peace officers to apprehend
and take into custody any minor found in violation of this chapter. The City
officer designated as the juvenile authority shall thereupon notify said parent
or guardian and such parent or guardian shall be immediately summoned.
   B.   Prosecution Against Parent: In any prosecution under this section
against the parent, guardian or other adult person having the care and custody
of a minor under said age, it shall not constitute a defense thereto that said
person did not have knowledge that such minor did loiter, idle, wonder, stroll
or drive, operate or ride in an automobile randomly, purposelessly or
aimlessly, in or on the public streets, highways, roads, alleys, parks,
playgrounds or other public grounds, other public places or other unsupervised
places, at any time between the aforementioned prohibited hours. (Ord. 178,
1958; amd. Ord. 178, 3-28-1966)
   C.   Violations:
      1.   Minor: Violations shall be handled in accordance with the Montana
Youth Court Act.
      2.   Parent: Violations of this section by any parent, guardian or other
adult care giver are designated as Municipal infractions as specified in title
1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 3
ANIMAL CONTROL 1
SECTION:
7-3-1: Administration
7-3-2: Running At Large
7-3-3: Impound Fee
7-3-4: Notice Of Impound
7-3-5: Rabies Control
7-3-6: Public Nuisance Animals
 
Notes
1 1. MCA § 7-23-101 et seq.
7-3-1: ADMINISTRATION:
   A.   City Pound: All enclosures within the limits of the City which are now
used by the City for the purpose of impounding animals running at large,
contrary to the provisions of this chapter, and all enclosures which shall
hereafter be established by the City Council or under its instructions by the
animal control officer for such purpose, are hereby declared to be the public
pounds of the City. Said pounds shall be under the care of the animal control
officer.
   B.   Report To City Council: The animal control officer shall render to the
City Council at the end of each month a statement under oath, of all money
received by him, and shall at the same time pay to the City Clerk-Treasurer all
fees, penalties and surplus of all proceeds of sales, and present to the City
Council with the statement aforesaid the City Clerk- Treasurer's statement
therefor. (Ord. 65, 1913; amd. 1999 Code)
7-3-2: RUNNING AT LARGE:
   A.   Unlawful: It shall be unlawful for the owner of any horse, mule, goat,
sheep, swine, potbellied pig, cattle, or livestock to allow or permit the same
to run at large within the limits of the City. Violations of this section are
designated as Municipal infractions as specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this
Code.
   B.   Impounding: No horse, mule, sheep, goat, swine, potbellied pig, any
cattle or livestock shall be permitted to run at large in the City at any time
and if found running at large in the City, each and every of such animals shall
be impounded in any common or public pound of said City from whence they shall
not be released until the owner or some person shall pay to the animal control
officer the fees and penalty hereinafter provided. It shall be the duty of the
animal control officer and all police officers to take up and impound any such
animal known to him or them to be running at large contrary to the provisions
of this chapter.
   C.   Care Of Impounded Animals: It shall be the duty of the animal control
officer to receive into the City Pound all animals brought there in pursuance
of any of the provisions of this chapter, to take proper care of and provide
proper sustenance for all animals impounded. (Ord. 65, 1913; amd. 1999 Code;
Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019; Ord. 2019-02, 1-13-2020)
7-3-3: IMPOUND FEE:
The impound fee shall be the prevailing rate of the facility used for
impounding. (1961 Code § 6-2-6; amd. Res. 1995-R67, 9-28-1995; 1999 Code)
7-3-4: NOTICE OF IMPOUND:
Upon determination of the owner, the City will provide reasonable notice of
impound. (Ord. 65, 1913; amd. 1999 Code)
7-3-5: RABIES CONTROL:
Rabies control shall be in accordance with Montana Code Annotated. (1999 Code)
7-3-6: PUBLIC NUISANCE ANIMALS:
   A.   A public nuisance animal is any animal that unreasonably annoys humans,
endangers the life or health of other animals or persons, or substantially
interferes with the rights of citizens, other than their owners, to the
enjoyment of life or property. A public nuisance animal shall include, but not
be limited to, any animal that:
      1.   Is repeatedly found at large;
      2.   Damages the property of persons other than its owner;
      3.   Repeatedly molests or intimidates pedestrians or passersby;
      4.   Repeatedly chases vehicles;
      5.   Repeatedly barks, howls, whines, or growls such that it disturbs the
quiet enjoyment of the neighborhood as documented by persons living or working
in the immediate vicinity of the dog:
         a.   For a period of more than ten (10) minutes between the hours of
ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) A.M.;
         b.   For a period of more than twenty (20) minutes between the hours
of seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. and ten o'clock (10:00) P.M.;
         c.   It shall be an absolute defense to such violation if the owner or
other person maintaining or harboring the dog proves by a preponderance of the
evidence that the primary reason the dog was barking, howling, whining, or
growling was that the dog was being provoked by a person or was otherwise being
incited, or was acting as a guide dog, hearing dog, service dog, work dog, or
guard dog;
      6.   Causes fouling of the air by odor and thereby creates unreasonable
annoyances or discomfort to neighbors or others in close proximity to the
premises where the animal is kept or harbored;
      7.   Attacks other animals or is found to otherwise be a menace to the
public health, welfare, or safety. (Ord. 2010-05, 2-14-2011)
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his/her possession,
ownership, maintenance or control, a public nuisance animal. Violations of this
section are designated as Municipal infractions as specified in title 1,
chapter 4 of this Code. In addition to the penalties provided in title 1,
chapter 4 of this Code, the court may require payment of all impoundment fees
and all reasonable costs incurred in providing necessary veterinary attention
and treatment for the subject animal and any and all other reasonable costs
incurred as a result of the violation and, depending upon the severity of the
offense, order that the animal be seized and destroyed. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-
2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 3
ANIMAL CONTROL
ARTICLE A. DOGS AND CATS 1
SECTION:
7-3A-1: Administration
7-3A-2: Possessor And Harborer Defined
7-3A-3: License And Vaccination Required
7-3A-4: License And Registration; Fee
7-3A-5: Tag And Collar Required
7-3A-6: Running At Large
7-3A-7: Impounding
7-3A-8: Vicious Dogs
7-3A-9: Prohibited And Unlawful Acts
7-3A-10: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. MCA § 7-23-4102.
7-3A-1: ADMINISTRATION:
   A.   Enforcement Officers; Designated: All references in this Article to
police officers, Chief of Police or to police shall mean such officers as shall
be employed by the City to enforce the laws of the City, whether direct City
employees or deputy sheriffs of any consolidated law enforcement agency
providing police services to the City. (Ord., 1-26-1976)
   B.   Authority Of Enforcement Officers: The City Animal Control Officer, or
if off duty or otherwise unavailable, the County Sheriff and his deputies, any
police officer, any City police officer or any other person lawfully appointed
and employed by the City Council for the purpose of enforcing this Article, is
empowered to take up and seize all dogs in violation of this Article and may
pursue such dogs or cats onto private property if a violation occurs in the
presence of said officers or appointees of the City Council; further, such
officers or employees of the City Council appointed to enforce this Article may
enter upon any private property in pursuit of a dog or cat suspected of being
infected with rabies or in an effort to apprehend any dog or cat directed by
order of the City Court to seize. Persons other than law enforcement officers,
appointed by the City Council to enforce the provisions of this Article, shall
have the same authority as a police officer to issue citations for violations
of this Article to any person deemed in violation and such citations shall
constitute a formal complaint when filed in the City Court, and shall be
answerable by the person charged in like manner to any citation issued by a
police officer charging a violation of the law. (Ord., 2-10-1986; amd. 1999
Code)
7-3A-2: POSSESSOR AND HARBORER DEFINED:
Any person who shall permit a dog to remain upon or about his premises for the
space of three (3) days shall be deemed a possessor or harborer of said dog and
for all purposes herein shall be treated as the owner of said dog. (Ord., 5-14-
1973)
7-3A-3: LICENSE AND VACCINATION REQUIRED:
Nothing herein contained shall excuse the owner, harborer or possessor of any
dog or cat within the corporate limits of the City from having vaccinated and
licensed such animals, regardless of where or how they are kept or maintained
within the City limits. (Ord., 5-14-1973)
7-3A-4: LICENSE AND REGISTRATION; FEE:
   A.   Dogs:
      1.   Required: It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, harbor or
maintain in the City any dog over five (5) months of age unless such dog is
duly registered and licensed as herein provided. Licenses shall be issued by
the City Clerk-Treasurer upon proof that the dog has been vaccinated against
rabies. An annual dog license must be purchased by the owner of each dog
between April 1 and April 30 of each year. (Ord. 97-04, 9-12-1997; amd. 1999
Code)
      2.   Fee Schedule:
         a.   Specified:
 
Description         Fee Per Year
Male dog            $5.00
Spayed female dog   5.00
Unspayed female dog 10.00
Unneutered male dog 10.00
 
         b.   After April 30: Fees for dog licenses issued after April 30 of
the current license year are as follows:
 
Description         Fee
Male dog            $10.00
Spayed female dog   10.00
Unspayed female dog 20.00
Unneutered male dog 20.00
 
      3.   Registration: Registration shall be in the form required by the City
Clerk-Treasurer to supply sufficient information to identify the dog and the
owner. The provisions of this subsection shall not apply to nonresidents having
dogs under restrain with the City less than fifteen (15) days.
      4.   New Residents: Fees for registration of dogs brought into the City
by new residents at any time after April 30 of the current license year will be
at the single rate stated in subsection A1a of this Section.
      5.   Guide Dogs: Guide dogs for the blind or otherwise handicapped
persons will be licensed without charge upon proof of vaccination as
hereinabove required. (Ord. 97-04, 9-12-1997)
   B.   Cats:
      1.   Required: It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, harbor or
maintain in the City any cat over six (6) months of age unless such cat is duly
registered and licensed as herein provided. Licenses shall be issued by the
City Clerk-Treasurer or the Animal Control Officer upon proof that the cat has
been vaccinated against rabies. An annual cat license, at the fee stated, must
be purchased by the owner of each cat between April 1 and April 30 of each
year. (Eff. 3-27-1972; amd. letter dated 6-13-1991; 1999 Code)
      2.   Fee Schedule: All cats, three dollars ($3.00) per year.
      3.   After April 30: Fees for cat licenses issued after April 30 of the
current license year are six dollars ($6.00) for all cats.
      4.   Registration: Registration provisions as to new residents or
temporary visitors to the City are the same with reference to cats as those
provisions regarding dogs provided in subsections A3 and A4 of this Section.
(Eff. 3-27-1972)
7-3A-5: TAG AND COLLAR REQUIRED:
Upon proper registration and payment of the license fee, the City Clerk-
Treasurer or Animal Control Officer will issue to the applicant a license
certificate and a metal tag. The shape of the tag shall be changed each year
and shall have stamped thereon the year for which it was issued and the number
corresponding to the number of the certificate. Every owner must provide each
dog with a substantial collar to which the license tag shall be affixed at all
times. Any dog found without a license tag shall be deemed to be not licensed.
In the event a dog tag is lost or destroyed, a duplicate shall be issued by the
City Clerk-Treasurer or Animal Control Officer upon presentation of an
affidavit to that effect, a receipt or duplicate receipt showing payment of the
license fee for the current year and payment of a replacement cost fee of fifty
cents ($0.50) for each such duplicate. License tags are not transferable from
one dog to another. No refund shall be made on a dog license fee because of the
death of the dog or the removal of the owner from the City before the
expiration of the license period. (Eff. 3-27-1972; amd. letter dated 4-7-1982;
letter dated 6-13-1991; 1999 Code)
7-3A-6: RUNNING AT LARGE:
   A.   At Large Defined: "At large" means off the premises of the owner,
harborer or possessor, and not then and there restrained by leash, cord, chain
or otherwise.
   B.   Prohibited:
      1.   If any dog or cat be found running at large within the City limits,
the owner, harborer or possessor of such animal shall be guilty of a violation
of this Section. It is no defense to a charge under this Section that the
owner, harborer or possessor of such animal was unaware the animal was at large
or that such animal was released from the owner's premises by overt act, error
or omission on the part of any person.
      2.   Policy: It is declared to be the public policy of the City Council
that no dog or cat be off the premises of its owner, harborer or possessor at
any time, unless leashed or otherwise restrained and that the owner, harborer
or possessor shall be held strictly liable therefor, regardless of the
circumstances which may contribute to or result in the violation.
   C.   Seizure; Impoundment: Any such animal running at large shall be seized
and impounded by the City enforcement authority or any other officer or
official designated by the City Council, and a complaint may be filed charging
the violation. (Ord., 11-22-1982)
   D.   Impound Fee: The owner, harborer or possessor of any impounded animal
seized pursuant to this Section, must pay a redemption fee of the prevailing
rate of the facility used for impounding. These fees shall be in addition to
any fines or costs assessed by the court upon conviction of the violation.
(Ord., 11-22-1982; amd. 1999 Code)
   E.   Redemption; License And Vaccination Required: No animal impounded for
being at large may be redeemed unless or until it is currently licensed and
vaccinated.
   F.   Unclaimed; Disposition:
      1.   No impounded animal will be destroyed after the expiration of
seventy two (72) hours impoundment, unless reasonable effort has been made to
notify the person responsible for such animal, if identity can reasonably be
determined.
      2.   If such animal is not redeemed from impoundment within seventy two
(72) hours, it shall be humanely destroyed, except as provided in subsection 7-
3A-7D2 of this Article. (Ord., 11-22-1982)
7-3A-7: IMPOUNDING:
   A.   Duty Of Officials: It shall be the duty of the Animal Control Officer
or other officers or persons appointed by the City Council for the purpose of
enforcing these laws, to take up and impound any dog found running at large,
whether licensed or not; if such dog shall not be redeemed as hereinafter
provided within seventy two (72) hours after such dog shall have been
impounded, it shall be the duty of the officers charged with enforcing these
regulations, or any other person duly appointed by the City Council for such
purpose, to put the said dog to death in a humane manner. (Res., 7-24-1978;
amd. 1999 Code)
   B.   Notice And Redemption: It is hereby declared the duty of every owner of
any dog to know its whereabouts at all times. In the event any dog is
impounded, the owner shall redeem the same within seventy two (72) hours,
without formal notice, or said dog shall be subject to disposal as hereinabove
provided. (Eff. 3-27-1972; amd. 1999 Code)
   C.   Release: Any dog so impounded will be released upon presentation to the
Animal Control Officer or other officers appointed to enforce these
regulations, proof that the dog is currently licensed and that the dog has had
a rabies shot within the current period recommended by the local veterinarians;
provided, if said dog has not been licensed and/or vaccinated within the period
required, the owner or interested party, in order to redeem the dog from
impoundment, must immediately make payment of the necessary amounts for
vaccination and/or license and said dog will not be released solely upon
payment of impoundment fees, as set forth hereinafter, unless license and
vaccination are both current. Any person, including members of the same
household, who, upon notification of impoundment of their dog, refuse to pay
impoundment fees, whether said dog be otherwise redeemed or not, will be barred
from obtaining any dog license thereafter, without subsequent specific approval
for the purpose of a dog license from the City Council. (Res., 7-24-1978; amd.
1999 Code)
   D.   Unclaimed; Disposition And Alternative:
      1.   Any dog impounded pursuant to the provisions of this Article not
redeemed within the time period provided herein, may be put to death in a
humane manner as provided above. (Res., 7-24-1978)
      2.   If an impounded dog is not redeemed within the time provided and any
other person shall desire to redeem said animal, they may do so by paying the
impoundment fees, plus licensing and vaccination fees for said animal. (Eff. 3-
27-1972)
   E.   Redemption Defined: "Redemption", as used in this Article, shall mean
not only payment of impoundment fees, but payment for license and/or
vaccination, if the same be required to redeem the dog. (Res., 7-24-1978)
7-3A-8: VICIOUS DOGS:
   A.   Defined:
      1.   Any dog which, in a vicious or terrorizing manner, approaches any
person or domestic animal in apparent attitude of attack;
      2.   Any dog with a known propensity, tendency or disposition to attack,
to cause injury or to otherwise endanger the safety of human beings or animals;
or
      3.   Any dog which bites, inflicts injury, assaults or otherwise attacks
a human being or domestic animal on public or private property.
   B.   Unlawful To Own And Possess: It shall be unlawful for any person to own
and possess a vicious dog within the City. Whenever a prosecution for this
offense is commenced under this section, the dog so involved may not be
redeemed, pursuant to the provisions of this article, while awaiting final
decision of the court as to the disposition to be made of such dog.
   C.   Disposition After Conviction Of Offense: Upon the trial of any offense
under this section, the court may, upon conviction and in addition to the usual
judgment of conviction, order the animal control officer or other authorized
personnel of the City to put the dog to death or may order such other
disposition of the dog as will protect the inhabitants of the City.
   D.   Nuisance Declared: Any dog which has bitten a person without
provocation or any dog that has a known propensity to attack or bite human
beings is hereby declared to be a nuisance and a menace to the public health
and safety and the dog may be taken up and impounded as provided in subsection
7-3A-7A of this article. (1999 Code)
7-3A-9: PROHIBITED AND UNLAWFUL ACTS:
   A.   Hindering Impoundment: No person shall hinder or molest the animal
control officer or any persons appointed to enforce this article, while such
persons are engaged in seizing or capturing and delivering any dog to the
pound. Any person who so interferes with any other person lawfully enforcing
the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon
conviction thereof, subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
   B.   Killing Licensed Dog; Depriving Of Tag: Any unauthorized person who
shall kill or cause to be killed any dog licensed as herein provided without
the consent of the owner or possessor thereof, or who deprives a licensed dog
of his collar or tag or who puts a registered tag on a dog not registered,
shall be deemed to have committed a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof,
subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Eff. 3-27-1972; amd. 1999 Code)
   C.   Dogs In City Parks: No dogs shall be permitted in the City parks,
except for seeing-eye dogs when being used for that purpose and dogs being used
in police work. This subsection imposes an absolute prohibition on dogs in the
City parks whether unrestrained or restrained. This prohibition does not
prohibit dogs in areas that are undeveloped parks. Dogs in the City parks are
deemed a nuisance and may be impounded; provided, that a permit for organized
obedience training or shows may be granted for use in designated areas of
designated parks on designated days. The permit shall be obtained from the
animal shelter for that particular event. The permit shall be in writing and
shall designate the park area within the park, the dates and duration. A fee,
as prescribed by City Council resolution, shall be collected for each permit
for each event. (Ord., 1-23-1989)
7-3A-10: PENALTY:
Except as provided for in this article, violations of this article are
designated as Municipal infractions as specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this
Code. The following violations shall be considered a misdemeanor and punishable
as set forth in this Code: a) owning or possessing a vicious dog, as defined in
section
7-3A-8 of this article, b) hindering impoundment, as defined in subsection 7-
3A-9A of this article, and c) killing a licensed dog, as defined in subsection
7-3A-9B of this article. (Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 4
FIREARMS AND WEAPONS 1
SECTION:
7-4-1: Defined
7-4-2: Discharge Of Firearms Prohibited
7-4-3: Carrying Of Concealed Weapons While Under The Influence
7-4-4: Carrying Weapons In City Facilities; Exceptions; Penalty
7-4-5: Screening For Weapons In City Facilities
7-4-6: Exceptions
 
Notes
1 1. MCA § 45-8-351.
7-4-1: DEFINED:
Unless otherwise defined in this City Code, all terms shall have the same
definition as those definitions in the current Montana Code Annotated.
 
BUILDING: Shall have the meaning prescribed in § 50-60-101, MCA.
          Any building or structure owned and occupied by the City, and any building
          or structure lead and occupied by the City where a governmental function,
          public service, or public event is held. The use of a City-owned or -leased
CITY      building or structure by employees or members of the public, even if for
FACILITY: limited periods of time, is considered continual occupation of the building
          or structure. "City Facility" included the grounds immediately adjacent to
          the City-owned or -leased buildings or structures, including pathways
          leading to entrances.
          Any weapon, including a starter gun, which will or is designed to or may
          readily be converted to expel a projective by the action of any explosive;
FIREARM:  the frame or receiver of any such weapon and any firearm muffler or firearm
          silencer; and includes without limitation a pistol, revolver, rifle,
          shotgun, air rifle, BB gun, or machine gun as defined in § 45-8-302, MCA.
          Any weapon other than a firearm and includes without limitation a bow/
          crossbow, dirk, dagger, slingshot, sword, cane, billy club, knuckles made
OTHER     of any metal or hard substance, throwing stars, nunchucks, knife having a
WEAPON:   blade four inches (4") long or longer, razor, not including a safety razor,
          a destructive device as defined in § 45-8-332(1), MCA, or any other deadly
          weapon or other article or instrument possessed with the purpose to commit
          a criminal offense. (Ord. 2021-04, - -2022)
 
7-4-2: DISCHARGE OF FIREARMS PROHIBITED:
For purposes of preserving public safety, the discharge of any firearm within
the City limits shall be unlawful, except when discharged by law enforcement
officers, military personnel or militia in the discharge of their duties; a
legally licensed rifle range or shooting gallery; anyone duly authorized or
permitted; or in the authorized performance of ceremonials. (Ord. 2021-04, 11-
-2021)
7-4-3: CARRYING OF CONCEALED WEAPONS WHILE UNDER INFLUENCE:
As provided in § 45-8-327, MCA, a person is prohibited from carrying a
concealed weapon, whether firearm or other weapon, while under the influence of
an intoxicating substance, regardless of whether the person holds a valid
permit to carry the concealed weapon. Violations of this section shall be
considered misdemeanors pursuant to City Ordinance
1-4-1. (Ord. 2021-04, 11- -2021)
7-4-4: CARRYING WEAPONS IN CITY FACILITIES; EXCEPTIONS; PENALTY:
   A.   The open carry of a firearms or other weapon or the carry of an
unpermitted concealed firearm or other weapon by any person in a city facility
is prohibited.
   B.   A person with a valid permit to carry a concealed weapon issued
pursuant to § 45-8-321 or § 45-8-329, MCA, is prohibited is restricted from
exercising that permit to carry a concealed firearm or other weapon in city
facilities as described in § 45-8-356, including secure areas of law
enforcement facilities owned and operated by the City and any courtroom or
other area used by court personnel, pursuant to a court order.
   C.   Nothing herein shall prohibit a presiding judge from designating peace
officers and other persons with authority to carry weapons in buildings in
which court is held to meet the security needs of the building or facility.
   D.   Except for a person issued a permit pursuant to § 45-8-321 or § 45-8-
329, MCA, a person commits the offense of carrying a concealed weapon in a
prohibited place when the person purposely or knowingly carries an unconcealed
firearm or other weapon or unpermitted concealed firearm or other weapon in
city facility in violation of this chapter.
   E.   Violations of this section shall be considered misdemeanors pursuant to
City Ordinance
1-4-1. (Ord. 2021-04, 11- -2021)
7-4-5: SCREENING FOR WEAPONS IN CITY FACILITIES:
The Mayor or City Council may determine the circumstances and locations where
screening for Firearms and Other Weapons is required and may establish
standards for such screening. City officials and employees acting within their
official capacities may deny entrance to a City Facility, subject to such
screening standards, to a person who: (i) possesses an openly visible firearm
or other weapon; (ii) possesses an unpermitted concealed firearm or other
weapon; or (iii) possesses a permitted concealed firearm or other weapon in
locations of city facilities that have been restricted pursuant to court order
or state law. The City may require proof of a valid permit to carry a concealed
weapon before allowing the carrying of a permitted concealed firearm or other
weapon in a city facility. Refusing to provide a City employee or official
proof of a valid permit to carry a concealed weapon is sufficient basis for
denial of entry to the city facility. Screening under this section applies to
all those excepted by any other provision of this chapter. (Ord. 2021-04, 11- -
2021)
7-4-6: EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   Exceptions For Authorized Use: Other than participation in any
screening provided under City Ordinance
7-4-5, the provisions of this chapter do not apply to: any peace office of the
state; any officer of the United States government authorized to carry a
concealed firearm or other weapon; any member of the armed services or reserve
forces of the United States or National Guard, while in the performance of
their official duties; a probation or parole officer authorized to carry a
Firearm under § 46-23-1002, MCA; an agent of the state department of justice;
or a person authorized by the chief of police to carry or possess an
unconcealed weapon on City property.
   B.   Exceptions By Permit: Any person duly authorized and granted a special
permit under this Section is not in violation of the provisions of this chapter
provided the permit is valid and the permit-holder complies with the terms of
the permit, submits to any weapons screening, and otherwise complies with all
applicable laws and regulations.
      1.   Issuance Of Permit: Upon receipt of proper application and fees, the
Mayor and City Council may, at its discretion, grant special permits for:
         a.   Shooting galleries, gun clubs and others for shooting in fixed
localities and under specified rules;
         b.   Legitimate displays of firearms at shows or other public
occasions;
         c.   Other education, events, displays, shows, exhibitions, or sales
as determined appropriate.
      2.   Such permits shall be in writing attested by the City Clerk-
Treasurer conforming to such requirements as the Mayor and City Council shall
demand, and the permit thus issued shall be subject to revocation at any time
by action of the Mayor and City Council. (Ord. 2021-04, 11- -2021)
CHAPTER 5
HUNTING
SECTION:
7-5-1: Hunting Restricted
7-5-1: HUNTING RESTRICTED:
The City Council has decided for the safety of the citizens and for the
protection of City property that the following conditions apply:
   A.   Unlawful To Hunt On City Property: It shall be unlawful for any person
to engage in any hunting activity for game and/or wildlife on any real property
owned by the City of Forsyth, except for the property located by Vananda.
   B.   Exceptions: Nothing in this section shall be considered to prohibit the
firing of a gun, pistol or other firearm when done in the lawful defense of the
person, property, or family or in the necessary enforcement of the law. (Ord.
2000-02, 4-26-2000, eff. 5-26-2000)
   C.   Violations; Penalty: Violations of this chapter are designated as
Municipal infractions as specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord.
2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019)
CHAPTER 6
VEHICLES ON PRIVATE PROPERTY 1
SECTION:
7-6-1: Definitions
7-6-2: Enforcement
7-6-3: Prohibited
7-6-4: Permitted In A Building
7-6-5: Repair
7-6-6: Person Responsible
7-6-7: Notice
7-6-8: Violation And Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. See title 5, chapter 7 of this code.
7-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following definitions shall apply in the interpretation and enforcement of
this chapter unless otherwise noted. When not inconsistent with the context,
words used in the present tense include the future, words in the plural number
include the singular number and words in the singular number include the plural
number.
ABANDONED, WRECKED, JUNKED OR DISMANTLED MOTOR VEHICLES: Any motor vehicle
described in 61-1-102, Montana Code Annotated, which does not have lawfully
affixed thereto both an unexpired license plate or plates and the condition of
which is wrecked, dismantled, inoperative, abandoned or discarded.
ABANDONED, WRECKED, JUNKED OR DISMANTLED VEHICLE: Any vehicle described in
"abandoned, wrecked, junked or dismantled motor vehicles" as defined herein
which is not being utilized for its manufactured or intended purpose and has
been discarded, abandoned, wrecked, junked, dismantled or partially dismantled,
including parts thereof.
ENFORCEMENT OFFICER: A peace officer or any city, state or federal department
or agency operating with arrest authority in Forsyth, Montana.
PERSON: Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or
organization of any kind.
PRIVATE PROPERTY: Any real property within the city that is privately owned.
VEHICLE: Every device in, upon, or by which any person or property may be
transported or drawn upon a public highway or upon private property, including
trailers, semitrailers, travel or camp trailers, as well as machinery used in
farming, logging, excavating, but not including mobile homes presently utilized
for human habitation. "Vehicle" shall not include motorbikes, motorcycles,
motor scooters, tractors, go-carts and golf carts. (Ord. 2003-06, 7-14-2003,
eff. 8-14-2003)
7-6-2: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Authority: The enforcement officer is authorized and directed to
enforce all the provisions of this chapter, and all enforcement agencies of the
city shall cooperate in this regard.
   B.   Right Of Entry: The enforcement officer will contact the owner of the
premises and the responsible person, if different from the owner, either in
writing or by telephone prior to entry upon an individual's property. The
purpose of this contact is to receive affirmative permission to be on the
property. If the enforcement officer does not acquire prior permission to enter
onto the property, the officer will immediately contact the owner and/or the
responsible person upon entry on private property to explain the purpose of the
visit and receive permission to remain on the premises to conduct the
legitimate business of the city. Any combination of: 1) a "No Trespassing" sign
and a gate or chain on private property, or 2) the securing of a gate or chain
(other than by a simple latching or closure device) shall be considered
controlling. Entry shall not be made upon such property without the express
permission of the property owner and/or the responsible person, or in response
to legal process (search warrant). No enforcement officer shall be required to
enter a posted or gated piece of property if the officer feels threatened,
intimidated, or otherwise in fear of his or her personal safety. (Ord. 2003-06,
7-14-2003, eff. 8-14-2003)
7-6-3: PROHIBITED:
No person shall park, store, keep, place, leave or permit the same, any
abandoned, wrecked, junked or dismantled motor vehicle or vehicle upon any
private property within the city limits for a period in excess of seventy two
(72) hours. The presence of any abandoned, wrecked, junked or dismantled
vehicle or motor vehicle, or parts thereof, upon private property as specified
in this chapter, is declared a public nuisance which shall be abated as such in
accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
This section shall not apply to any vehicles enclosed within a building, or
covered by a fabric cover specifically designed for covering vehicles or motor
vehicles or to any vehicle held in connection with a business enterprise
lawfully licensed and properly operated in an appropriate zone, pursuant to the
zoning laws of the city or a vehicle in an appropriate storage place or
depository maintained in a lawful place and manner by the city or to any
vehicle or motor vehicle validly and properly retained by the owner thereof for
antique collection purposes, pursuant to 61-3-411, Montana Code Annotated.
Any motor vehicle whether in operable or inoperable condition designed, adapted
or used for drag strip racing or raceway racing shall be covered, as set forth
in this chapter, or placed within a building. (Ord. 2003-06, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-
14-2003)
7-6-4: PERMITTED IN A BUILDING:
Storage, service, restoration and repair of an abandoned, wrecked, junked or
dismantled vehicle or motor vehicle which is conducted within the confines of a
building shall be permitted provided that such vehicle or motor vehicle is the
property of the owner or occupier of the lot and provided that the storage
service, service, restoration or repair is not a commercial use of the
property. (Ord. 2003-06, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-14-2003)
7-6-5: REPAIR:
This chapter shall not be construed to prevent any occupant of a premises
within the city limits from repairing his own motor vehicles or vehicle or
machinery on his premises even though exposed to public view, so long as the
person pursues the work to completion with reasonable diligence; provided,
however, that any vehicle which remains out of running condition with any
wheel, tire, engine, body or other major part removed therefrom for a period in
excess of twenty (20) days, while remaining exposed to public view, shall be
deemed to be prima facie evidence that the vehicle or motor vehicle is not
being diligently repaired and constitutes a violation of this chapter. (Ord.
2003-06, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-14-2003)
7-6-6: PERSON RESPONSIBLE:
The owner of any private property within the city limits shall be absolutely
responsible for any violation of this chapter. (Ord. 2003-06, 7-14-2003, eff.
8-14-2003)
7-6-7: NOTICE:
Whenever it comes to the attention of the enforcement officer that a nuisance
exists within the city limits due to the maintenance or presence of abandoned,
wrecked, junked or dismantled motor vehicles or vehicles upon private property
within the city limits, a notice in writing shall be served upon the occupant
of the land where the nuisance exists, or in the case there is no such
occupant, then upon the person being the owner of the property, notifying them
of the existence of the nuisance and ordering its removal in the time specified
in this chapter.
   A.   Notice shall be given by United States mail, postage prepaid, addressed
to the occupant or the person who is the owner at the last known address as
exists upon the records of the city. An alternative notice may be served in the
same manner as other legal process is served in the state.
   B.   The enforcement officer shall give the notice for the removal of the
items that constitute the nuisance at least ten (10) days before the time of
compliance with the notice. The notice shall specify clearly the abandoned,
wrecked, junked or dismantled motor vehicles or vehicles, or parts thereof upon
the private property, which constitutes the nuisance and shall order the
removal of the same as specified within this chapter. The notice shall advise
that failure to remove or cover as specified in the notice shall render the
person so served subject to prosecution for violation of this chapter and the
penalty therefor as set forth in this chapter. The notice shall contain the
name, address and telephone number of the enforcement officer for contact by
the occupant or owner. (Ord. 2003-06, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-14-2003)
7-6-8: VIOLATION AND PENALTY:
   A.   Failure of the person or persons responsible for the removal or
covering of abandoned, wrecked, junked or dismantled motor vehicles or vehicles
or parts thereof to remove or cover the same within the time specified in the
notice, after the same has been served as provided in this chapter, constitutes
a violation of this chapter. Any person violating any provision of this chapter
shall be subject to a penalty as provided in section
1-4-2 of this Code.
   B.   In any action or proceeding brought for the violation of this chapter,
as defined in this chapter, the reasonable cost and expense to City in
connection with the mailing or serving of notice and the inspection of the
private property in question, shall be awarded to City as part of the court's
sentence.
   C.   Violations of this chapter are designated as Municipal infractions as
specified in title 1, chapter 4 of this Code. (Ord. 2003-06, 7-14-2003, eff. 8-
14-2003; amd. Ord. 2018-05, 11-19-2018, eff. 1-1-2019; Ord. 2019-02, 1-13-2020)
CHAPTER 7
PUBLIC USE AND DISPLAY OF MARIJUANA
SECTION:
7-7-1: Purpose And Intent
7-7-2: Definitions
7-7-3: Public Display, Smoking Or Consumption Of Marijuana Prohibited
7-7-4: State Law Superseded And Applicable
7-7-5: Violation And Penalty
7-7-6: No Private Right Of Action
7-7-1: PURPOSE AND INTENT:
The purpose of this chapter is to identify acts regarding the use of marijuana
within the city of Forsyth that are not authorized to be conducted in a manner
open or visible to the general public. (Ord. 2010-04, 9-28-2010; amd. Ord.
2022-02, 6-13-2022)
7-7-2: DEFINITIONS:
 
MARIJUANA:                           Has the meaning provided in Montana Code
                                     Annotated section 16-12-102.
                                     The uses of marijuana described in Montana
                                     Code Annotated section 50-46-102(5). Other
MEDICAL MARIJUANA:                   phrases herein such as the use of medical
                                     marijuana or the medical use of marijuana
                                     shall have the same meaning and includes
                                     the term "usable marijuana."
                                     Any highway, road, driveway, alley, lane,
                                     parking area, sidewalk, park, trail, or
                                     other public or private place within the
WAYS OF THE CITY OPEN TO THE PUBLIC: city of Forsyth that is adapted and fitted
                                     for the use of the public and that is in
                                     common use by the public. (Ord. 2010-04,
                                     9-28-2010; amd. Ord. 2022-02, 6-13-2022)
 
7-7-3: PUBLIC DISPLAY, SMOKING OR CONSUMPTION OF MARIJUANA PROHIBITED:
No person authorized by title 50, chapter 46, or title 16. chapter 12. Montana
Code Annotated, to acquire, possess, cultivate, manufacture, deliver, transfer
or transport marijuana may on the ways of the city open to the public display,
smoke or consume marijuana in an open or visible manner. A violation of this
section is an absolute liability offense. (Ord. 2010-04, 9-28-2010; amd. Ord.
2022-02, 6-13-2022)
7-7-4: STATE LAW SUPERSEDED AND APPLICABLE:
The provisions of this chapter shall supersede title 50, chapter 46, and title
16, chapter 12, Montana Code Annotated, only insofar as this chapter expands
the limitations on the use of marijuana. All other provisions of state law
related to medical marijuana shall be applicable. (Ord. 2010-04, 9-28-2010;
amd. Ord. 2022-02, 6-13-2022)
7-7-5: VIOLATION AND PENALTY:
A violation of this chapter is a misdemeanor and upon conviction a person shall
be fined not more than five hundred dollars ($500.00) or imprisoned in the
Rosebud County Jail for a period not to exceed six (6) months or both. A person
so convicted shall also be required to pay all costs and expenses of
prosecution and the courts as authorized by law. (Ord. 2010-04, 9-28-2010; amd.
Ord. 2022-02, 6-13-2022)
7-7-6: NO PRIVATE RIGHT OF ACTION:
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to create right of action regarding
the acquisition, possession, cultivation, manufacture, delivery, transfer, or
transport of either marijuana or medical marijuana. (Ord. 2010-04, 9-28-2010;
amd. Ord. 2022-02, 6-13-2022)
CHAPTER 8
MARIJUANA BUSINESSES PROHIBITED
SECTION:
7-8-1: Definitions
7-8-2:    Marijuana Businesses Prohibited
7-8-3:    Penalties
7-8-1: DEFINITIONS:
In addition to all other definitions cited in this title, which are
specifically incorporated herein by reference, the following definitions apply:
              A licensed premises from which a person licensed by the
              department may obtain marijuana or marijuana products from a
ADULT-USE     licensed cultivator, manufacturer, dispensary, or other
DISPENSARY:   licensee approved under this chapter; and sell marijuana or
              marijuana products to registered cardholders, adults that are
              twenty one (21) years of age or older, or both.
COMBINED-USE  A licensee possessing both a tier I canopy license and one
MARIJUANA     dispensary license from the department allowing for the
LICENSEE:     operation of a dispensary.
              A person licensed by the department to plant, cultivate, grow,
              harvest, and dry marijuana; and package and re-label marijuana
CULTIVATOR:   produced at the location in a natural or naturally dried form
              that has not been converted, concentrated, or compounded for
              sale through a licensed dispensary.
DEPARTMENT:   The Department of Revenue provided for in M.C.A. § 2-15-1301.
              A person licensed by the department to convert or compound
MANUFACTURER: marijuana into marijuana products, marijuana concentrates, or
              marijuana extracts and package, repackage, label, or relabel
              marijuana products as allowed under this chapter.
              All plant material from the genus Cannabis containing
              tetrahydrocannabinol (THC) or seeds of the genus capable of
              germination. The term does not include hemp, including any part
              of that plant, including the seeds and all derivatives,
              extracts, cannabinoids, isomers, acids, salts, and salts of
              isomers, whether growing or not, with a delta-
              9 tetrahydrocannabinol concentration of not more than 0.3% on a
MARIJUANA:    dry weight basis, or commodities or products manufactured with
              hemp, or any other ingredient combined with marijuana to
              prepare topical or oral administrations, food, drink or other
              products.
              The term also does not include a drug approved by the United
              States Food and Drug Administration pursuant to Section 505 of
              the Federal Food, Drug, and Cosmetic Act, 21 U.S.C. §§ 301 et
              seq.
              A cultivator, manufacturer, adult-use dispensary, medical
MARIJUANA     marijuana dispensary, combined-use marijuana licensee, testing
BUSINESS:     laboratory, marijuana transporter, or any other business or
              function that is licensed by the department.
MARIJUANA     Any type of marijuana product consisting wholly or in part of
CONCENTRATE:  the resin extracted from any part of the marijuana plant.
MARIJUANA     Any mixture or preparation of the dried leaves, flowers, resin,
DERIVATIVE:   or byproducts of the marijuana plant, including but not limited
              to marijuana concentrates and other marijuana products.
              A product that contains marijuana and is intended for use by a
MARIJUANA     consumer by a means other than smoking. The term includes but
PRODUCT:      is not limited to edible products, ointments, tinctures,
              marijuana derivatives, and marijuana concentrates.
              A person that is licensed to transport marijuana and marijuana
              products from one marijuana business to another marijuana
MARIJUANA     business, or to and from a testing laboratory, and to
TRANSPORTER:  temporarily store the transported retail marijuana and retail
              marijuana products at its licensed premises but is not
              authorized to sell marijuana or marijuana products to consumers
              under any circumstances.
MEDICAL       Marijuana or marijuana products that are for sale solely to a
MARIJUANA:    cardholder who is registered under Title 16, chapter 12, part 5
              of Montana Code Annotated.
MEDICAL       The location from which a registered cardholder may obtain
MARIJUANA     marijuana or marijuana products.
DISPENSARY:
              A qualified person, licensed by the department that provides
TESTING       testing of representative samples of marijuana and marijuana
LABORATORY:   products; and provides information regarding the chemical
              composition and potency of a sample, as well as the presence of
              molds, pesticides, or other contaminants in a sample.
 
(Ord. 2022-05, passed by voters on 11-8-2022)
7-8-2: MARIJUANA BUSINESSES PROHIBITED:
As authorized by HB 701, Section 59 and M.C.A. § 16-12-301(7)(a), and based
upon the November 8, 2022, election results, marijuana businesses are
prohibited from opening or operating within the limits of the City of Forsyth.
(Ord. 2022-05, passed by voters on 11-8-2022)
7-8-3: PENALTIES:
Violations of this Chapter are civil municipal infractions within the exclusive
jurisdiction of the City Court of the City of Forsyth. Violations are
punishable by a civil penalty of not more than five hundred dollars ($500.00)
or imprisoned in the Rosebud County Jail for a period not to exceed six (6)
months or both. A person so convicted shall also be required to pay all costs
and expenses of prosecution and the courts as authorized by law.
(Ord. 2022-05, passed by voters on 11-8-2022)

Violations of this title are designated as Municipal infractions as specified

CHAPTER 1
STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
8-1-1: Emergency Temporary Street Closures
8-1-1: EMERGENCY TEMPORARY STREET CLOSURES:
There is hereby adopted that for all times the emergency help helicopter,
servicing Rosebud Healthcare Center, is required to be grounded for the loading
or unloading of passengers, the sections of Park Street and 18th Avenue,
immediately adjacent to the Rosebud Healthcare Center, in the city of Forsyth,
Montana, shall be closed to all motorized vehicles. Gates shall be constructed
and closed for safety purposes. The street closures shall not exceed a total
period of three (3) hours. Said regulations shall be enforced by any remedy
available in law or equity. (Ord. 02-2012, 2-13-2012)
ARTICLE A. SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION 1
SECTION:
8-1A-1: Administration And Enforcement
8-1A-2: Permit Required
8-1A-3: Public Liability And Property Damage Insurance
8-1A-4: Construction Requirements
8-1A-5: Concrete Curbing; Exception
8-1A-6: Placement Of Sidewalks
8-1A-7: Access Ramp For Handicapped Persons
8-1A-8: Duties Of Property Owner To Keep Sidewalks Repaired
8-1A-9: Contract For Construction
8-1A-10: Payment For Construction
8-1A-11: Payment For Repairs
8-1A-12: Assessments
 
Notes
1 1. MCA § 7-14-4122.
8-1A-1: ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT:
It shall be the duty of the building inspector, in all cases where he may find
any person engaged in the work of constructing sidewalks, to ascertain at once
if such person has a permit to perform such work and, in the event of such
person not having a permit, to cause them to cease work until proper
application has been made and a permit issued. (Ord. 2015-07, 11-9-2015)
8-1A-2: PERMIT REQUIRED:
No person shall construct any sidewalks on any of the streets or avenues of the
city without a permit in writing. Application for permits may be made by the
parties employed to construct the work or by the owners of the property, and
must state the location, the name of the owner, the number of the lot and block
abutting upon the sidewalk to be built. (Ord. 171, 7-18-1951; amd. 1999 Code)
8-1A-3: PUBLIC LIABILITY AND PROPERTY DAMAGE INSURANCE:
Before any contractor shall be granted a permit to construct sidewalks in the
city, he shall file with the city clerk- treasurer a policy in such amount as
the city council shall deem necessary; also that he will indemnify and save
harmless the city from all suits, accidents and damages consequent thereupon
for or by reason of any opening in the streets and walks made by him or those
in his employ, or any such damages due to any act of the contractor or those in
his employ, by reason of the performance of such construction work. No bond
shall be required from the owner of any lot who wishes to actually construct
the walk himself. (Ord. 171, 7-18-1951)
8-1A-4: CONSTRUCTION REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Order Of City Council: Whenever in the judgment of the city council, a
sidewalk or curb shall be constructed in front of any lot or parcel of land
within the city it shall, by majority vote, order the construction of the same.
The order shall be entered upon the minutes of the city council, shall name the
street or avenue along which said sidewalk or curb is to be constructed and
shall specify the general character of material of which such sidewalk or curb
shall be constructed.
   B.   Notice: Thereafter, the city clerk-treasurer shall cause to be
published in one issue of the official newspaper of the city a notice that the
city council has ordered the construction of a sidewalk or curb, giving the
description of the lot or parcel of land in front of which a sidewalk or curb
is to be constructed, which notice shall state that if the owners or agents of
the owners of lots or parcels of land in front of which such sidewalks or curbs
are to be constructed, shall fail for a period of thirty (30) days after the
date of the publication of such notice to cause such sidewalks or curbs to be
constructed, the city will cause such sidewalks or curbs to be constructed and
will assess the cost thereof against the property in front of which the same is
constructed. On or before the second day following the date of publication of
said notice, the city clerk-treasurer shall mail a copy thereof to the owner or
agent of the owner of each lot or parcel of land in front of which a sidewalk
or curb has been ordered constructed as specified in said notice. (Ord. 171, 7-
18-1951)
   C.   Failure To Comply; Performance By City: If the owner or agent of the
owner of any lot or parcel of land in front of which any sidewalk or curb shall
be ordered constructed shall fail or neglect, during such period of thirty (30)
days, to construct such sidewalk or curb, the city council may cause the same
to be constructed by the letting of a contract for the construction thereof to
the lowest responsible bidder, after advertising for bids for the construction
thereof, or upon failure to receive an acceptable bid, may order the city to
construct such sidewalk or curb. (Ord. 171, 7-18-1951; amd. 1999 Code)
8-1A-5: CONCRETE CURBING; EXCEPTION:
All curbs and curbing constructed or placed on the line of any street or avenue
within the city shall be of concrete or other such material as may be approved
by the building inspector, with the consent and approval of the city council,
such curbing to be constructed according to plans and specifications in the
office of the building inspector, provided however, that with the consent of
the city council, the building inspector may give a permit authorizing the
construction of temporary wooden curbs in outlying portions of the city. When
any curbing now in existence shall be renewed or repaired, the same shall be
done in compliance with the terms hereof. (Ord. 2015-07, 11-9-2015)
8-1A-6: PLACEMENT OF SIDEWALKS:
Placement of sidewalks, whether new, reconstructed or replacing existing
sidewalks, will remain consistent and in line with other sidewalks in the same
block. If no sidewalks are present in the block, placement of the first
sidewalk designates placement of all other sidewalks for that block. (Ord. 97-
07, 10-27-1997, eff. 11-27-1997)
8-1A-7: ACCESS RAMP FOR HANDICAPPED PERSONS:
   A.   Required; Design: All new sidewalk and curb constructed after the
effective date hereof or all reconstructed curbing and sidewalk, occurring at a
pedestrian crossing within the city, will contain, at appropriate locations,
wheelchair ramps according to the standard design required as set forth in
state statute. (Res., 6-28-1976, eff. 7-28-1976; amd. 1999 Code)
   B.   Compliance Required: It shall be the responsibility of all individuals
constructing such sidewalks or curbs at pedestrian crossings within the city or
any private or public contractors, so constructing such sidewalks and/or curbs
in violation hereof, as well as the owners of any real property upon which such
sidewalks and/or curbs are constructed at pedestrian crossings, to comply with
this section. (Res., 6-28-1976, eff. 7-28-1976)
   C.   Noncompliance; Performance By City: In the event of noncompliance, the
building inspector or mayor may issue an order in writing to the owner of such
property, extending to said owner thirty (30) days in which to remedy and
correct the violation. In the event the owner shall fail to correct and remedy
the violation by reconstructing said sidewalk and/or curb to conform to this
section, the city is thereupon authorized to proceed, through the use of city
employees and city furnished materials, to reconstruct said sidewalk and/or
curb to conform to this section and all such reasonable charges for labor and
materials so used by the city shall be immediately payable by the owner to the
city. Such charges for material and labor shall additionally bear interest at
the legal rate after the date of billing until paid and may be assessed against
the owner of said property as a tax upon the property and may be collected in
the same manner as other taxes of the city are collected. This provision for
collection shall not limit the city to any other remedy available under law for
collection of this debt. (Ord. 2015-07, 11-9-2015)
8-1A-8: DUTIES OF PROPERTY OWNER TO KEEP SIDEWALKS REPAIRED:
It is the duty of the owner(s) of any premises within the city to keep the
sidewalks in front of and adjoining their premises in good safe and substantial
condition and repair, and that the owner(s) shall see that all breaks and
unsoundness of any character resulting from natural deterioration or from any
other cause whatever are repaired with all possible dispatch. (Ord. 2003-08,
11-10-2003, eff. 12-10-2003)
8-1A-9: CONTRACT FOR CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Specifications; Insurance: If the construction of such sidewalk or curb
is done by contract after advertisement for bids, such advertisement for bids
and contract may be for sidewalks or curbs in front of one or more lots or
parcels of land as the city council shall determine. All sidewalks and curbs
constructed by the city shall be constructed in accordance with specifications
therefor prepared by the city engineer. Any contract to whom a contract is let
for the construction of sidewalks or curbs shall, before commencing work,
execute and deliver to the city public liability and property damage insurance
as provided in this article 1 .
   B.   Lowest Responsible Bidder; Bond: The city council may, if it sees fit,
at any time let to the lowest responsible bidder after advertising for bids, a
contract for the construction of all sidewalk and curbs, for a period of not to
exceed one year, which may be ordered constructed under the provisions of this
article and which have not been constructed by the owner or agent of the owner
of the property, such construction to be in accordance with specifications
prepared therefor by the city engineer and such contractor, before he commences
any work under his contract, shall be required to deliver to the city a good
and sufficient bond for which sum as may be determined by the city council,
which bond shall be conditioned for the faithful performance of all work done
by him under the provisions of such contract and such specifications.
   C.   Authority To Proceed: Should the contract mentioned in the preceding
subsection be entered into, such contractor shall, within ten (10) days after
being notified to do so by the city engineer, proceed with the construction of
any sidewalks or curbs previously ordered by the city council, which have not
been constructed by the owner or agent of the owner, and shall, within forty
five (45) days thereafter, fully complete the construction thereof in
accordance with his contract and the specifications for such work prepared by
the city engineer, and that once such construction work has been commenced, the
same shall thereafter be prosecuted with due diligence until completed. (Ord.
171, 7-18-1951)
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  8-1A-3 of this article.
8-1A-10: PAYMENT FOR CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Fund Created: There is hereby created a fund to be known as the special
sidewalk and curb fund, in which fund shall be kept all assessments and taxes
collected pursuant to the resolutions levying an assessment and tax referred to
in section
8-1A-11 of this article, which fund shall be expended by the city clerk-
treasurer for the purpose of paying warrants issued thereon, whenever such fund
is sufficient to pay any of such warrants. (Ord. 2015-07, 11-9-2015)
8-1A-11: PAYMENT FOR REPAIRS:
All repairs to sidewalks made by the city shall be paid out of the general
fund, and the city clerk-treasurer shall keep a separate account of the cost of
such repairs and charge the abutting property therewith, and shall certify a
list of all property chargeable with repairs of sidewalks, with the amount of
the cost of repairs for which each separate parcel is chargeable, to which cost
he shall add interest at the rate of six percent (6%) per annum from the date
of the incurring of such charge by the city, and ten percent (10%) additional
to cover costs and charges of administration, and such items shall constitute a
tax against the property affected thereby, and such tax shall be collected or
the property sold for delinquency as in the case of special improvement
assessments, and all taxes collected under the provisions of this article shall
be placed in the general fund. (Ord. 171, 7-18-1951; amd. 1999 Code)
8-1A-12: ASSESSMENTS:
   A.   Authority: The cost and expense of the construction of any sidewalk or
curb caused to be constructed by the city council under the provisions of this
article shall be assessed against the lot or parcel of land in front of which
such sidewalk or curb is constructed. (Ord. 171, 7-18-1951)
   B.   Resolution Levying And Assessing: The city council shall annually and
before the later of the first Thursday after the first Tuesday in September or
thirty (30) days from the receipt of the certified taxable value; each year,
pass and adopt a resolution levying and assessing a tax against each lot or
parcel of land in front of which sidewalks or curbs have been caused to be
constructed under the provisions of this article, which resolution shall be in
every manner prepared and certified the same as resolutions levying assessments
for the making of improvements in special improvement districts. (Ord. 2015-07,
11-9-2015)
   C.   Payment; Term: (Rep. by Ord. 2015-07, 11-9-2015)
   D.   Collection: The city clerk-treasurer or the county treasurer, as the
case may be, shall collect the special assessment or tax levied by the city
council under the provisions of this article with interest as herein provided,
such interest to run from the date of the registry of the warrant and the city
clerk-treasurer shall at any time permit the owner of any property assessed for
sidewalk or curb constructed under the provisions of this article to pay the
cost and expenses of construction with interest to the date of payment.
   E.   Lien: The cost and expenses of the construction of sidewalks and curbs
under the provisions of this article shall be a lien upon the lot or parcel of
land in front of which the same is constructed and when any one of the payments
assessed and levied by the city council shall become delinquent, the property
against which the same is levied and assessed shall be sold by the city clerk-
treasurer, the same as the sale of property for nonpayment of assessments and
levies for the making of improvements in special improvement districts. (Ord.
171, 7-18-1951)
   F.   Nonpayment Of Property Assessments: Anytime the city is required,
either through their employees, or to a contractor to resolve, remedy, or
otherwise abate a condition in which the property owner is in violation of the
city, the owner is billed for such repair, and the owner does not pay the bill
within sixty (60) calendar days of the notice, failure to pay will be
considered nonpayment. Nonpayment shall be a considered lien against the
property, and is enforceable in the same manner as nonpayment of property taxes
is enforced.
In the event the property owner who is billed objects or challenges to the
amount of the bill, or any other issues related to the bill, they may request
to be placed upon the agenda at a regularly scheduled city council meeting at
any time before the expiration of the sixty (60) day period. (Ord. 2001-02, 12-
27-2001, eff. 1-27-2002)
CHAPTER 2
EXCAVATIONS
SECTION:
8-2-1: Permission And Bond Required
8-2-2: Application
8-2-3: Excavation Fees
8-2-4: Excavation Of Trenches
8-2-5: Warning Devices
8-2-6: Refilling Of Excavations Or Trenches
8-2-1: PERMISSION AND BOND REQUIRED:
   It shall be unlawful for any person to make an excavation of any kind,
nature or description in the streets or alleys of the city without first
obtaining permission of the Water/Waste Water Director or public works director
and posting a bond in such an amount or sum as may be fixed by the city council
protecting the same city from any damage that might or could result from the
